 introduction 

 in give to the world the record of what , look at as an adventure 
 only , be I suppose one of the most wonderful and mysterious experience

 my exact connection with it be . and so I may as well say at once that I 
 be not the narrator but only the editor of this extraordinary history , 
 and then go on to tell how it find its way into my hand . 

 some year ago I , the editor , be stop with a friend , " vir 
 doctissimus et amicus neus , " at a certain University , which for the 
 purpose of this history we will call Cambridge , and be one day much 
 strike with the appearance of two person whom I see go arm - in - arm 
 down the street . one of these gentleman be I think , without exception , 
 the handsome young fellow I have ever see . he be very tall , very 
 broad , and have a look of power and a grace of bearing that seem as 
 native to he as it be to a wild stag . in addition his face be almost 
 without flaw - a good face as well as a beautiful one , and when he lift 
 his hat , which he do just then to a pass lady , I see that his head 
 be cover with little golden curl grow close to the scalp . 

 " good gracious ! " I say to my friend , with whom I be walk , " why , 
 that fellow look like a statue of Apollo come to life . what a splendid 
 man he be ! " 

 " yes , " he answer , " he be the handsome man in the University , and one 
 of the nice too . they call he ' the greek god ' ; but look at the other

 I will introduce you , " and he do , and for some minute we stand 
 chat - about the Zulu people , I think , for I have just return from

 fair - haired girl , and these two Mr. Vincey , who clearly know they well ,

 fellow .

 " - - College , Cambridge , May 1 , 18 - 

 " my dear Sir , - you will be surprised , consider the very slight nature

 well begin by remind you that we once meet , now some five year ago ,

 this letter , as may be imagine , astonish I considerably , but when I 
 come to look at the MS . , which the pressure of other work prevent I

 reader will be also , and at once make up my mind to press on with the

 stamp of truth upon its face . its explanation I must leave to other , 
 and with this slight preface , which circumstance make necessary , I 
 introduce the world to Ayesha and the Caves of K"r . - the Editor . 

 P.S. - there be on consideration one circumstance that , after a reperusal 
 of this history , strike I with so much force that I can not resist

 matter ? be that ancient Kallikrates nothing but a splendid animal

 see , perceive the germ and smoulder spark of greatness which lie hid

 here also I be not able to answer , but must leave the reader to form his

 this remark will doubtless strike anybody who read it as be slightly

 " now , " she say , " if I be Beauty , who be you ? " that be when I be only 
 twenty . 

 and so I stand and star , and feel a sort of grim satisfaction in the

 the year ROLL by 

 as might be expect , poor Vincey 's sudden death create a great stir 
 in the College ; but , as he be know to be very ill , and a satisfactory 
 doctor 's certificate be forthcoming , there be no inquest . they be

 in a very little while   for , as I expect , I get my fellowship   the

 the child grow into the boy , and the boy into the young man , while one

 the SHERD of amenartas 

 on the day precede Leo 's twenty - fifth birthday we both journey to

 Job touch his head , not have a hat on .

 he obey , and from the box I take the key that poor Vincey , Leo 's

 " now be you both ready ? " I say , as people do when they be go to

 it be , or appear to be , of ebony , or some such close - grain black

 actually commence to crumble from age . 

 " now for it , " I say , insert the second key .

 dinte with age , but otherwise in fairly sound condition . 

 I draw it out and set it on the table , and then , in the midst of the 
 most perfect silence , I insert the strange - look silver key , and

 have never be able to discover . this I carefully remove to the depth

 modern - look envelope , and address in the handwriting of my dead

 " to my son Leo , should he live to open this casket . " 

 I hand the letter to Leo , who glance at the envelope , and then put it 
 down upon the table , make a motion to I to go on empty the casket . 

 the next thing that I find be a parchment carefully roll up . I

 but into black - letter Latin , which at the first glance from the style

 of the sixteenth century . immediately beneath this roll be something 
 hard and heavy , wrap up in yellow linen , and repose upon another

 linen , expose to view a very large but undoubtedly ancient potsherd 
 of a dirty yellow colour ! this potsherd have in my judgment , once be 
 a part of an ordinary amphora of medium size . for the rest , it measure

 towards the bottom of the box with write in the later uncial greek 
 character , fade here and there , but for the most part perfectly

 great care , and by mean of a reed pen , such as the ancient

 wonderful fragment have be break in two , and rejoin by mean of 
 cement and eight long rivet . also there be numerous inscription on

 clearly be make by different hand and in many different age , and 
 of they , together with the writing on the parchment , I shall have to 
 speak presently .

 " my Son Leo , - when you open this , if you ever live to do so , you will 
 have attain to manhood , and I shall have be long enough dead to

 " and now , " Leo go on , without reply , " enough of myself . what have to 
 be say belong to you who live , not to I , who be dead , and almost as

 and take a strong hold in my imagination . when I be only nineteen year

 about the time of Elizabeth , to investigate its truth . into all that 
 befell I I can not enter now . but this I see with my own eye . on the

 at the extremity of which a peak tower up , shape like the head of a

 " of the adventure that befell I after this I need not now speak . I be

 story be at an end . 

 " for you , however , my son , it be not at an end , and to you I hand on 
 these the result of my labour , together with the hereditary proof of 
 its origin . it be my intention to provide that they shall not be put 
 into your hand until you have reach an age when you will be able to

 brain . 

 " I do not believe that it be a fable ; I believe that if it can only

 visibly exist . life exist ; why therefore should not the mean of 
 preserve it indefinitely exist also ? but I have no wish to prejudice

 terrible , not as the proverb would infer , from the inherent superstition

 to they . and if the end be attain , if at last you emerge from the

 above the natural decay of flesh and intellect , who shall say that the 
 awesome change would prove a happy one ? Choose , my son , and may the 
 Power who rule all thing , and who say ' thus far shalt thou go , and 
 thus much shalt thou learn , ' direct the choice to your own happiness

 experience . - farewell ! " 

 thus the letter , which be unsigned and undated , abruptly end .

 " well , let us see what the potsherd have to say , at any rate , " say Leo , 
 take up the translation in his father 's writing , and commence to

 " I , Amenartas , of the Royal House of the Pharaohs of Egypt , wife of 
 Kallikrates   the Beautiful in Strength , a Priest of Isis whom the 
 god cherish and the demon obey , be about to die , to my little son 
 tisisthene   the Mighty Avenger . I flee with thy father from Egypt in 
 the day of Nectanebes ,     cause he through love to break the vow 
 that he have vow . we flee southward , across the water , and we wander 
 for twice twelve moon on the coast of Libya   Africa   that look towards 
 the rise sun , where by a river be a great rock carven like the head 
 of an Ethiopian . four day on the water from the mouth of a mighty river 
 be we cast away , and some be drown and some die of sickness . but 
 we wild man take through waste and marsh , where the sea fowl hide the 
 sky , bear we ten day ' journey till we come to a hollow mountain , 
 where a great city have be and fall , and where there be cave of 
 which no man hath see the end ; and they bring we to the Queen of the 
 people who place pot upon the head of stranger , who be a magician 
 have a knowledge of all thing , and life and loveliness that do not 
 die . and she cast eye of love upon thy father , Kallikrates , and would 
 have slay I , and take he to husband , but he love I and fear she , 
 and would not . then do she take we , and lead we by terrible way , by 
 mean of dark magic , to where the great pit be , in the mouth of which 
 the old philosopher lie dead , and show to we the rolling Pillar of 
 life that die not , whereof the voice be as the voice of thunder ; and 
 she do stand in the flame , and come forth unharmed , and yet more 
 beautiful . then do she swear to make thy father undye even as she be , 
 if he would but slay I , and give himself to she , for I she could

 prevail thus far against she . and he hold his hand before his eye to 
 hide her beauty , and would not . then in her rage do she smite he by 
 her magic , and he die ; but she weep over he , and bear he thence with 
 lamentation : and be afraid , I she send to the mouth of the great 
 river where the ship come , and I be carry far away on the ship 
 where I give thee birth , and hither to Athens I come at last after many 
 wandering . now I say to thee , my son , tisisthene , seek out the woman , 
 and learn the secret of Life , and if thou mayest find a way slay she , 
 because of thy father Kallikrates ; and if thou dost fear or fail , this 
 I say to all thy seed who come after thee , till at last a brave man be 
 find among they who shall bathe in the fire and sit in the place of the 
 Pharaohs . I speak of those thing , that though they be past belief , yet 
 I have know , and I lie not . " 

      Nekht - nebf , or Nectanebo II . , the last native Pharaoh of

 the english translation be , as I discover on further investigation , 
 and as the reader may easily see by comparison , both accurate and 
 elegant . 

 besides the uncial writing on the convex side of the sherd at the top , 
 paint in dull red , on what have once be the lip of the amphora , be 
 the cartouche already mention as be on the scarabæus , which we 
 have also find in the casket . the hieroglyphic or symbol , however , 
 be reverse , just as though they have be press on wax . whether this 
 be the cartouche of the original Kallikrates ,     or of some Prince or 
 Pharaoh from whom his wife Amenartas be descend , I be not sure , nor 
 can I tell if it be draw upon the sherd at the same time that the 
 uncial Greek be inscribe , or copy on more recently from the Scarab 
 by some other member of the family . nor be this all . at the foot of 
 the writing , paint in the same dull red , be the faint outline of a 
 somewhat rude drawing of the head and shoulder of a Sphinx wear 
 two feather , symbol of majesty , which , though common enough upon the 
 effigy of sacred bull and god , I have never before meet with on a 
 Sphinx . 

      the cartouche , if it be a true cartouche , can not have 
  be that of Kallikrates , as Mr. Holly suggest . kallikrate 
  be a priest and not entitle to a cartouche , which be the 
  prerogative of egyptian royalty , though he might have 
  inscribe his name or title upon an oval . - Editor . 

 also on the right - hand side of this surface of the sherd , paint

 in EARTH and SKIE and SEA

 HOC FECIT

 perfectly bewilder , I turn the relic over . it be cover from top

 be address . it be , " I could not go . tisisthene to his son ,

 between these two ancient writing , the second of which be inscribe

 the next legible thing after the greek signature be the word 
 " Romae , A.U.C. , " show that the family have now migrate to Rome . 
 unfortunately , however , with the exception of its termination   evi   the 
 date of their settlement there be for ever lose , for just where it have

 then follow twelve latin signature , jot about here and there , 
 wherever there be a space upon the tile suitable to their inscription . 
 these signature , with three exception only , end with the name 
 " Vindex " or " the Avenger , " which seem to have be adopt by the 
 family after its migration to Rome as a kind of equivalent to the greek 
 " tisisthene , " which also mean an avenger . ultimately , as might be 
 expect , this latin cognoman of Vindex be transform first into De 
 Vincey , and then into the plain , modern Vincey . it be very curious 
 to observe how the idea of revenge , inspire by an Egyptian who live 
 before the time of Christ , be thus , as it be , embalm in an English 
 family name .

 after the roman name there be evidently a gap of very many century . 
 nobody will ever know now what be the history of the relic during those 
 dark age , or how it come to have be preserve in the family . my 
 poor friend Vincey have , it will be remember , tell I that his roman 
 ancestor finally settle in Lombardy , and when Charlemagne invade 
 it , return with he across the Alps , and make their home in Brittany , 
 whence they cross to England in the reign of Edward the Confessor . how 
 he know this I be not aware , for there be no reference to lombardy or 
 Charlemagne upon the tile , though , as will presently be see , there be a 
 reference to Brittany . to continue : the next entry on the sherd , if I 
 may except a long splash either of blood or red colour matter of 
 some sort , consist of two cross draw in red pigment , and probably 
 represent Crusaders ' sword , and a rather neat monogram   " D. V. " 
 in scarlet and blue , perhaps execute by that same Dorothea Vincey who 
 write , or rather paint , the doggrel couplet . to the left of this , 
 inscribe in faint blue , be the initial A. V. , and after they a date , 
 1800 . 

 then come what be perhaps as curious an entry as anything upon this 
 extraordinary relic of the past . it be execute in black letter , write 
 over the cross or Crusaders ' sword , and date fourteen hundred and 
 forty - five . as the good plan will be to allow it to speak for itself , I 
 here give the black - letter fac - simile , together with the original Latin 
 without the contraction , from which it will be see that the writer 
 be a fair mediæval latinist . also we discover what be still more 
 curious , an english version of the black - letter Latin . this , also 
 write in black letter , we find inscribe on a second parchment that 
 be in the coffer , apparently somewhat old in date than that on which 
 be inscribe the mediæval latin translation of the uncial Greek of 
 which I shall speak presently . this I also give in full . 

  Fac - simile of Black - Letter Inscription on the Sherd of Amenartas . 

 " Iſta reliq ia eſt valde miſticu   et myrificu   op s q d maiore 
 mei ex Armorica ſſ Brittania mi ore ſecu   co veheba t et q dm 
 ſc s cleric s ſe per p ri meo in manu ferebat q d pe itus illvd 
 deſtrueret , affirma s q d eſſet ab ipſo ſathana co flatu 
 preſtigioſa et dyabolica arte q re p ter mevs co fregit illvd 
 I   dvas p tes q s q dm ego Johs   de Vi ceto ſalvas ſervavi et 
 adaptavi ſicut ap paret die lu e p r   poſt feſt beate Mrie vir g 
 anni gr e mccccxlv . " 

  Expanded Version of the above Black - Letter Inscription . 

 " ista reliquia est valde misticum et myrificum opus , quod majores mei 
 ex Armorica , scilicet Britannia Minore , secum convehebant ; et et quidam 
 sanctus clericus semper patri meo in manu ferebat quod penitus illud 
 destrueret , affirmans quod esset ab ipso Sathana conflatum prestigiosa 
 et dyabolica arte , quare pater meus confregit illud in duas parte , quas 
 quidem ego Johannes de Vinceto salvas servavi et adaptavi sicut apparet 
 die lune proximo post festum beate Marie Virginis anni gratie MCCCCXLV . " 

  Fac - simile of the Old English Black - Letter Translation of the above 
 Latin Inscription from the Sherd of Amenartas find inscribe upon a 
 parchment . 

 " Thys rellike ys a ryghte mistycall worke    a marvaylous yᵉ whyche 
 myne auncetere afore tyme dyd conveigh hider wᵗ yᵐ ffrom Armoryke 
 whᵉ ys to ſeien Britaine yᵉ leſſe    a certayne holye clerke 
 ſhoulde allweye beare my ffadir on honde yᵗ he owghte uttirly ffor 
 to ffruſſhe yᵉ ſame affyrmynge yᵗ yt be ffourmyd    confflatyd 
 off ſathanas hym ſelffe by arte magike    dyvellyſſhe wherefore my 
 ffadir dyd take yᵉ ſame    to braſt yt yn tweyne but I John de Vincey 
 dyd ſave whool yᵉ tweye p tes therof    topeecyd yᵐ togydder agayne 
 ſoe as yee ſe on y s   daye mondaye next ffolowynge after yᵉ ffeeste 
 of ſeynte Marye yᵉ bleſſed vyrgyne yn yᵉ yeere of ſalvacioun 
 ffowertene hundreth    ffyve    ffowrti . " 

  Modernised Version of the above Black - Letter Translation . 

 " Thys rellike ys a ryghte mistycall worke and a marvaylous , ye whyche 
 myne auncetere aforetyme dyd conveigh hider with they from Armoryke 
 which ys to seien Britaine ye Lesse and a certayne holye clerke should 
 allweye beare my fadir on honde that he owghte uttirly for to frusshe 
 ye same , affyrmynge that yt be fourme and conflatye of Sathanas hym 
 selfe by arte magike and dyvellysshe wherefore my fadir dyd take ye same 
 and tobrast yt yn tweyne , but I , John de Vincey , dyd save whool ye tweye 
 part therof and topeecyd they togydder agayne soe as yee se , on this 
 daye mondaye next followynge after ye feeste of Seynte Marye ye bless 
 Vyrgyne yn ye yeere of Salvacioun fowertene hundreth and fyve and 
 fowerti . " 

 the next and , save one , last entry be Elizabethan , and date 1564 . " a 
 most strange historie , and one that do cost my father his life ; for in 
 seekynge for the place upon the east coast of Africa , his pinnance 
 be sink by a portuguese galleon off Lorenzo Marquez , and he himself 
 perish . - John Vincey . " 

 then come the last entry , apparently , to judge by the style of 
 writing , make by some representative of the family in the middle of the 
 eighteenth century . it be a misquotation of the well - know line in 
 Hamlet , and run thus : " there be more thing in Heaven and earth than 
 be dream of in your philosophy , Horatio . "   

      another thing that make I fix the date of this entry 
  at the middle of the eighteenth century be that , curiously 
  enough , I have an act copy of " Hamlet , " write about 
  1740 , in which these two line be misquote almost exactly 
  in the same way , and I have little doubt but that the Vincey 
  who write they on the potsherd hear they so misquoted at 
  that date . of course , the line really run : - 

  there be more thing in heaven and earth , Horatio , 
  than be dream of in your philosophy . - L. H. H. 

 and now there remain but one more document to be examine - namely , the 
 ancient black - letter transcription into mediæval Latin of the uncial 
 inscription on the sherd . as will be see , this translation be execute 
 and subscribe in the year 1495 , by a certain " learn man , " Edmundus 
 de Prato   Edmund Pratt   by name , licentiate in Canon Law , of Exeter 
 College , Oxford , who have actually be a pupil of Grocyn , the first 
 scholar who teach Greek in England .     no doubt , on the fame of this 
 new learning reach his ear , the Vincey of the day , perhaps that same 
 John de Vincey who year before have save the relic from destruction and 
 make the black - letter entry on the sherd in 1445 , hurry off to 
 Oxford to see if perchance it might avail to dissolve the secret of 
 the mysterious inscription . nor be he disappoint , for the learn 
 Edmundus be equal to the task . indeed his rendering be so excellent 
 an example of mediæval learning and latinity that , even at the risk of 
 sate the learn reader with too many antiquity , I have make up my 
 mind to give it in fac - simile , together with an expand version for the 
 benefit of those who find the contraction troublesome . the translation 
 have several peculiarity on which this be not the place to dwell , but I 
 would in pass call the attention of scholar to the passage " duxerunt 
 autem nos ad reginam advenaslasaniscoronantium , " which strike I as 
 a delightful rendering of the original , " ἤγαγον δὲ ὡς 
 βασίλειαν τὴν τῶν ξένους χύτραις 
 στεφανούντων . " 

      Grocyn , the instructor of Erasmus , study Greek under 
  Chalcondylas the Byzantine at Florence , and first lecture 
  in the Hall of Exeter College , Oxford , in 1491 . - Editor .

  Expanded Version of the above Mediæval Latin Translation 

 Amenartas , e genere regio Egyptii , uxor Callicratis , sacerdotis Isidis , 
 quam dei fovent demonia attendunt , filiolo suo Tisistheni jam moribunda 
 ita mandat : Effugi quodam ex Egypto , regnante Nectanebo , cum patre tuo , 
 propter mei amorem pejerato . fugiente autem versus Notum trans mare , 
 et viginti quatuor mense per litora Libye versus Orientem errante , 
 ubi est petra quedam magna sculpta instar Ethiopis capitis , deinde die 
 quatuor ab ostio fluminis magni ejecti partim submersi sumus partim 
 morbo mortui sumus : in fine autem a feris hominibus portabamur per 
 palude et vada , ubi avium multitudo celum obumbrat , die decem , donec 
 advenimus ad cavum quendam montem , ubi olim magna urb erat , caverne 
 quoque immense ; duxerunt autem nos ad reginam Advenaslasaniscoronantium , 
 que magicâ utebatur et peritiá omnium rerum , et saltem pulcritudine et 
 vigore insenescibilis erat . Hec magno patris tui amore perculsa , 
 primum quidem ei connubium michi mortem parabat ; postea vero , recusante 
 Callicrate , amore mei et timore regine affecto , nos per magicam abduxit 
 per via horribile ubi est puteus ille profundus , cuju juxta aditum 
 jacebat senioris philosophi cadaver , et advenientibus monstravit 
 flammam Vite erectam , instar columne voluntantis , vox emittentem quasi 
 tonitrus : tunc per ignem impetu nocivo expers transiit et jam ipsa sese 
 formosior visa est . 

 Quibus factis juravit se patrem tuum quoque immortalem ostensuram 
 esse , si me prius occisa regine contubernium mallet ; neque enim ipsa I 
 occidere valuit , propter nostratum magicam cuju egomet partem habeo . 
 Ille vero nichil hujus generis malebat , manibus ante oculo passis , ne 
 mulieris formositatem adspiceret : postea illum magica percussit arte , 
 at mortuum efferebat inde cum fletibus et vagitibus , et I per timorem 
 expulit ad ostium magni flumini , velivoli , porro in nave , in qua te 
 peperi , vix post die huc Athenas vecta sum . at tu , o tisisthene , ne 
 quid quorum mando nauci fac : necesse enim est mulierem exquirere si qua 
 Vite mysterium impetre et vindicare , quautum in te est , patrem tuum 
 Callieratem in regine morte . sin timore sue aliqua causa rem reliquis 
 infectam , hoc ipsum omnibus posteris mando , dum bonus quis inveniatur 
 qui ignis lavacrum non perhorrescet , et potentia dignus dominabitur 
 hominum . 

 Talia dico incredibilia quidem at minime ficta de rebus michi cognitis . 

 Hec Grece scripta Latine reddidit vir doctus Edmundus de Prato , in 
 Descretis Licenciatus , e Collegio Exoniensi Oxoniensi doctissimi Grocyni 
 quondam e pupilli , Idibus Aprilis Anno Domini MCCCCLXXXXV . 

 " well , " I say , when at length I have read out and carefully examine 
 these writing and paragraph , at least those of they that be still 
 easily legible , " that be the conclusion of the whole matter , Leo , and 
 now you can form your own opinion on it . I have already form mine . " 

 " and what be it ? " he ask , in his quick way . 

 " it be this . I believe that potsherd to be perfectly genuine , and that , 
 wonderful as it may seem , it have come down in your family from since 
 the fourth century before Christ . the entry absolutely prove it , and 
 therefore , however improbable it may seem , it must be accept . but 
 there I stop . that your remote ancestress , the egyptian princess , or 
 some scribe under her direction , write that which we see on the sherd 
 I have no doubt , nor have I the slight doubt but that her suffering 
 and the loss of her husband have turn her head , and that she be not 
 right in her mind when she do write it . " 

 " how do you account for what my father see and hear there ? " ask Leo . 

 " Coincidence . no doubt there be bluff on the coast of Africa that 
 look something like a man 's head , and plenty of people who speak bastard 
 Arabic . also , I believe that there be lot of swamp . another thing 
 be , Leo , and I be sorry to say it , but I do not believe that your poor 
 father be quite right when he write that letter . he have meet with 
 a great trouble , and also he have allow this story to prey on his 
 imagination , and he be a very imaginative man . anyway , I believe that 
 the whole thing be the most unmitigated rubbish . I know that there be 
 curious thing and force in nature which we rarely meet with , and , when 
 we do meet they , can not understand . but until I see it with my own eye , 
 which I be not likely to , I never will believe that there be any mean 
 of avoid death , even for a time , or that there be or be a white 
 sorceress live in the heart of an african swamp . it be bosh , my boy , 
 all bosh ! - what do you say , Job ? " 

 " I say , sir , that it be a lie , and , if it be true , I hope Mr. Leo will not 
 meddle with no such thing , for no good can not   come of it . " 

 " perhaps you be both right , " say Leo , very quietly . " I express no 
 opinion . but I say this . I be go to set the matter at rest once and 
 for all , and if you will not   come with I I will go by myself . " 

 I look at the young man , and see that he mean what he say . when Leo 
 mean what he say he always put on a curious look about the mouth . it 
 have be a trick of his from a child . now , as a matter of fact , I have no 
 intention of allow Leo to go anywhere by himself , for my own sake , if 
 not for his . I be far too attached to he for that . I be not a man 
 of many tie or affection . circumstance have be against I in this 
 respect , and man and woman shrink from I , or at least , I fancy that 
 they do , which come to the same thing , think , perhaps , that my 
 somewhat forbidding exterior be a key to my character . rather than 
 endure this , I have , to a great extent , seclude myself from the world , 
 and cut myself off from those opportunity which with most man result 
 in the formation of relation more or less intimate . therefore Leo be 
 all the world to I - brother , child , and friend - and until he weary of 
 I , where he go there I should go too . but , of course , it would not do 
 to let he see how great a hold he have over I ; so I cast about for some 
 mean whereby I might let myself down easy . 

 " yes , I shall go , Uncle ; and if I do not   find the ' rolling Pillar of 
 Life , ' at any rate I shall get some first - class shooting . " 

 here be my opportunity , and I take it . 

 " shooting ? " I say . " ah ! yes ; I never think of that . it must be a very 
 wild stretch of country , and full of big game . I have always want to 
 kill a buffalo before I die . do you know , my boy , I do not   believe in the 
 quest , but I do believe in big game , and really on the whole , if , after 
 think it over , you make up your mind to go , I will take a holiday , 
 and come with you . " 

 " ah , " say Leo , " I think that you would not lose such a chance . but 
 how about money ? we shall want a good lot . " 

 " you need not trouble about that , " I answer . " there be all your income 
 that have be accumulate for year , and besides that I have save 
 two - third of what your father leave to I , as I consider , in trust for 
 you . there be plenty of cash . " 

 " very well , then , we may as well stow these thing away and go up to 
 town to see about our gun . by the way , Job , be you come too ? it be 
 time you begin to see the world . " 

 " well , sir , " answer Job , stolidly , " I do not   hold much with foreign 
 part , but if both you gentleman be go you will want somebody to 
 look after you , and I be not the man to stop behind after serve you 
 for twenty year . " 

 " that be right , Job , " say I. " you will not   find out anything wonderful , but 
 you will get some good shooting . and now look here , both of you . I will not 
 have a word say to a live soul about this nonsense , " and I point 
 to the potsherd . " if it get out , and anything happen to I , my next of 
 kin would dispute my will on the ground of insanity , and I should become 
 the laugh stock of Cambridge . " 

 that day three month we be on the ocean , bind for Zanzibar . 



 IV 

 the SQUALL 

 how different be the scene that I have now to tell from that which have 
 just be tell ! go be the quiet college room , go the wind - sway 
 english elm , the caw rook , and the familiar volume on the shelf , 
 and in their place there rise a vision of the great calm ocean gleaming 
 in shade silver light beneath the beam of the full african moon . a 
 gentle breeze fill the huge sail of our dhow , and draw we through 
 the water that ripple musically against her side . Most of the man be 
 sleep forward , for it be near midnight , but a stout swarthy Arab , 
 mahome by name , stand at the tiller , lazily steer by the star . 
 three mile or more to our starboard be a low dim line . it be the 
 eastern shore of Central Africa . we be run to the southward , before 
 the North East Monsoon , between the mainland and the reef that for 
 hundred of mile fringe this perilous coast . the night be quiet , so 
 quiet that a whisper can be hear fore and aft the dhow ; so quiet that a 
 faint boom sound roll across the water to we from the distant land . 

 the Arab at the tiller hold up his hand , and say one word : - " simba 
  lion ! " 

 we all sit up and listen . then it come again , a slow , majestic sound , 
 that thrill we to the marrow . 

 " to - morrow by ten o'clock , " I say , " we ought , if the Captain be not out 
 in his reckoning , which I think very probable , to make this mysterious 
 rock with a man 's head , and begin our shooting . " 

 " and begin our search for the ruin city and the Fire of Life , " 
 correct Leo , take his pipe from his mouth , and laugh a little . 

 " nonsense ! " I answer . " you be air your Arabic with that man at 
 the tiller this afternoon . what do he tell you ? he have be trade 
  slave - trading , probably   up and down these latitude for half of his 
 iniquitous life , and once land on this very ' man ' rock . do he ever 
 hear anything of the ruin city or the cave ? " 

 " no , " answer Leo . " he say that the country be all swamp behind , and 
 full of snake , especially python , and game , and that no man live 
 there . but then there be a belt of swamp all along the east African 
 coast , so that do not go for much . " 

 " yes , " I say , " it do - it go for malaria . you see what sort of an 
 opinion these gentry have of the country . not one of they will go with 
 we . they think that we be mad , and upon my word I believe that they be 
 right . if ever we see old England again I shall be astonish . however , 
 it do not greatly matter to I at my age , but I be anxious for you , 
 Leo , and for Job . it be a Tom Fool 's business , my boy . " 

 " all right , Uncle Horace . so far as I be concern , I be willing to take 
 my chance . look ! what be that cloud ? " and he point to a dark blotch 
 upon the starry sky , some mile astern of we . 

 " go and ask the man at the tiller , " I say . 

 he rise , stretch his arm , and go . presently he return . 

 " he say it be a squall , but it will pass far on one side of we . " 

 just then Job come up , look very stout and english in his 
 shooting - suit of brown flannel , and with a sort of perplexed appearance 
 upon his honest round face that have be very common with he since he 
 get into these strange water . 

 " please , sir , " he say , touch his sun hat , which be stick on to the 
 back of his head in a somewhat ludicrous fashion , " as we have get all 
 those gun and thing in the whale - boat astern , to say nothing of the 
 provision in the locker , I think it would be good if I get down and 
 sleep in she . I do not   like the look "   here he drop his voice to a 
 portentous whisper   " of these black gentry ; they have such a wonderful 
 thievish way about they . suppose now that some of they be to slip 
 into the boat at night and cut the cable , and make off with she ? that 
 would be a pretty go , that would . " 

 the whale - boat , I may explain , be one specially build for we at Dundee , 
 in Scotland . we have bring it with we , as we know that this coast be a 
 network of creek , and that we might require something to navigate 
 they with . she be a beautiful boat , thirty - foot in length , with a 
 centre - board for sailing , copper - bottomed to keep the worm out of she , 
 and full of water - tight compartment . the Captain of the dhow have tell 
 we that when we reach the rock , which he know , and which appear to 
 be identical with the one describe upon the sherd and by Leo 's father , 
 he would probably not be able to run up to it on account of the shallow 
 and breaker . therefore we have employ three hour that very morning , 
 whilst we be totally becalm , the wind have drop at sunrise , 
 in transfer most of our good and chattel to the whale - boat , 
 and place the gun , ammunition , and preserve provision in the 
 water - tight locker specially prepared for they , so that when we do 
 sight the fabled rock we should have nothing to do but step into the 
 boat , and run she ashore . another reason that induce we to take this 
 precautionary step be that arab captain be apt to run past the point 
 that they be make , either from carelessness or owe to a mistake in 
 its identity . now , as sailor know , it be quite impossible for a dhow 
 which be only rig to run before the monsoon to beat back against it . 
 therefore we get our boat ready to row for the rock at any moment . 

 " well , Job , " I say , " perhaps it would be as well . there be lot of 
 blanket there , only be careful to keep out of the moon , or it may turn 
 your head or blind you . " 

 " Lord , sir ! I do not   think it would much matter if it do ; it be that 
 turn already with the sight of these blackamoor and their filthy , 
 thieving way . they be only fit for muck , they be ; and they smell bad 
 enough for it already . " 

 Job , it will be perceive , be no admirer of the manner and custom of 
 our dark - skin brother . 

 accordingly we haul up the boat by the tow - rope till it be right 
 under the stern of the dhow , and Job bundle into she with all the grace 
 of a fall sack of potato . then we return and sit down on the deck 
 again , and smoke and talk in little gust and jerk . the night be so 
 lovely , and our brain be so full of suppress excitement of one sort 
 and another , that we do not feel inclined to turn in . for nearly an 
 hour we sit thus , and then , I think , we both doze off . at least I have 
 a faint recollection of Leo sleepily explain that the head be not a 
 bad place to hit a buffalo , if you could catch he exactly between the 
 horn , or send your bullet down his throat , or some nonsense of the 
 sort . 

 then I remember no more ; till suddenly - a frightful roar of wind , a 
 shriek of terror from the awakening crew , and a whip - like sting of water 
 in our face . some of the man run to let go the haulyard and lower the 
 sail , but the parrel jam and the yard would not come down . I spring 
 to my foot and hang on to a rope . the sky aft be dark as pitch , but the 
 moon still shine brightly ahead of we and light up the blackness . beneath 
 its sheen a huge white - top breaker , twenty foot high or more , be 
 rush on to we . it be on the break - the moon shine on its crest and 
 tip its foam with light . on it rush beneath the inky sky , drive by 
 the awful squall behind it . suddenly , in the twinkling of an eye , I see 
 the black shape of the whale - boat cast high into the air on the crest of 
 the break wave . then - a shock of water , a wild rush of boiling foam , 
 and I be cling for my life to the shroud , ay , sweep straight out 
 from it like a flag in a gale . 

 we be poope . 

 the wave pass . it seem to I that I be under water for 
 minute - really it be second . I look forward . the blast have tear out 
 the great sail , and high in the air it be flutter away to leeward 
 like a huge wound bird . then for a moment there be comparative calm , 
 and in it I hear Job 's voice yell wildly , " come here to the boat . " 

 Bewildered and half - drown as I be , I have the sense to rush aft . I 
 feel the dhow sink under I - she be full of water . under her counter 
 the whale - boat be toss furiously , and I see the Arab Mahomed , who 
 have be steer , leap into she . I give one desperate pull at the 
 tow - rope to bring the boat alongside . wildly I spring also , Job catch 
 I by the arm and I roll into the bottom of the boat . down go the 
 dhow bodily , and as she do so Mahomed draw his curved knife and sever 
 the fibre - rope by which we be fast to she , and in another second we 
 be drive before the storm over the place where the dhow have be . 

 " Great God ! " I shriek , " where be Leo ? Leo ! Leo ! " 

 " he be go , sir , God help he ! " roar Job into my ear ; and such be the 
 fury of the squall that his voice sound like a whisper . 

 I wring my hand in agony . Leo be drown , and I be leave alive to 
 mourn he . 

 " look out , " yell Job ; " here come another . " 

 I turn ; a second huge wave be overtake we . I half hop that it 
 would drown I . with a curious fascination I watch its awful advent . 
 the moon be nearly hide now by the wreath of the rush storm , but 
 a little light still catch the crest of the devouring breaker . there 
 be something dark on it - a piece of wreckage . it be on we now , and 
 the boat be nearly full of water . but she be build in air - tight 
 compartment - Heaven bless the man who invent they ! - and lift up 
 through it like a swan . through the foam and turmoil I see the black 
 thing on the wave hurry right at I . I put out my right arm to ward 
 it from I , and my hand close on another arm , the wrist of which my 
 finger grip like a vice . I be a very strong man , and have something 
 to hold to , but my arm be nearly tear from its socket by the strain and 
 weight of the float body . have the rush last another two second I 
 might either have let go or go with it . but it pass , leave we up 
 to our knee in water . 

 " bail out ! bail out ! " shout Job , suit the action to the word . 

 but I could not bail just then , for as the moon go out and leave we in 
 total darkness , one faint , fly ray of light light upon the face of the 
 man I have grip , who be now half lie , half float in the bottom 
 of the boat . 

 it be Leo . Leo bring back by the wave - back , dead or alive , from the 
 very jaw of Death . 

 " bail out ! bail out ! " yell Job , " or we shall founder . " 

 I seize a large tin bowl with a handle to it , which be fix under one 
 of the seat , and the three of we bail away for dear life . the furious 
 tempest drive over and round we , fling the boat this way and that , 
 the wind and the storm wreath and the sheet of sting spray blind 
 and bewilder we , but through it all we work like demon with the 
 wild exhilaration of despair , for even despair can exhilarate . one 
 minute ! three minute ! six minute ! the boat begin to lighten , and no 
 fresh wave swamp we . five minute more , and she be fairly clear . 
 then , suddenly , above the awful shrieking of the hurricane come a 
 duller , deep roar . Great Heavens ! it be the voice of breaker ! 

 at that moment the moon begin to shine forth again - this time behind the 
 path of the squall . out far across the torn bosom of the ocean shoot the 
 ragged arrow of her light , and there , half a mile ahead of we , be a 
 white line of foam , then a little space of open - mouthed blackness , and 
 then another line of white . it be the breaker , and their roar grow 
 clear and yet more clear as we speed down upon they like a swallow . 
 there they be , boil up in snowy spout of spray , smite and 
 gnash together like the gleam tooth of hell . 

 " take the tiller , Mahomed ! " I roar in Arabic . " we must try and shoot 
 they . " at the same moment I seize an oar , and get it out , motion to 
 Job to do likewise . 

 mahome clamber aft , and get hold of the tiller , and with some 
 difficulty Job , who have sometimes pull a tub upon the homely cam , get 
 out his oar . in another minute the boat 's head be straight on to the 
 ever - near foam , towards which she plunge and tear with the speed 
 of a racehorse . just in front of we the first line of breaker seem 
 a little thin than to the right or leave - there be a cap of rather 
 deep water . I turn and point to it . 

 " steer for your life , Mahomed ! " I yell . he be a skilful steersman , 
 and well acquaint with the danger of this most perilous coast , and I 
 see he grip the tiller , bend his heavy frame forward , and stare at the 
 foaming terror till his big round eye look as though they would start 
 out of his head . the send of the sea be drive the boat 's head round 
 to starboard . if we strike the line of breaker fifty yard to starboard 
 of the gap we must sink . it be a great field of twisting , spouting 
 wave . Mahomed plant his foot against the seat before he , and , 
 glance at he , I see his brown toe spread out like a hand with the 
 weight he put upon they as he take the strain of the tiller . she come 
 round a bit , but not enough . I roar to Job to back water , whilst I 
 drag and labour at my oar . she answer now , and none too soon . 

 Heavens , we be in they ! and then follow a couple of minute of 
 heart - break excitement such as I can not hope to describe . all that I 
 remember be a shriek sea of foam , out of which the billow rise here , 
 there , and everywhere like avenge ghost from their ocean grave . once 
 we be turn right round , but either by chance , or through Mahomed 's 
 skilful steering , the boat 's head come straight again before a breaker 
 fill we . one more - a monster . we be through it or over it - more 
 through than over - and then , with a wild yell of exultation from the 
 Arab , we shoot out into the comparative smooth water of the mouth of sea 
 between the tooth - like line of gnashing wave . 

 but we be nearly full of water again , and not more than half a mile 
 ahead be the second line of breaker . again we set to and bail 
 furiously . fortunately the storm have now quite go by , and the moon 
 shine brightly , reveal a rocky headland run half a mile or more 
 out into the sea , of which this second line of breaker appear to be 
 a continuation . at any rate , they boil around its foot . probably the 
 ridge that form the headland run out into the ocean , only at a low 
 level , and make the reef also . this headland be terminate by a curious 
 peak that seem not to be more than a mile away from we . just as we get 
 the boat pretty clear for the second time , Leo , to my immense relief , 
 open his eye and remark that the clothe have tumble off the bed , 
 and that he suppose it be time to get up for chapel . I tell he to 
 shut his eye and keep quiet , which he do without in the slight 
 degree realize the position . as for myself , his reference to chapel 
 make I reflect , with a sort of sick longing , on my comfortable room 
 at Cambridge . why have I be such a fool as to leave they ? this be a 
 reflection that have several time recur to I since , and with an 
 ever - increase force . 

 but now again we be drift down on the breaker , though with 
 lessen speed , for the wind have fall , and only the current or the 
 tide   it afterwards turn out to be the tide   be drive we . 

 another minute , and with a sort of howl to Allah from the Arab , a pious 
 ejaculation from myself , and something that be not pious from Job , 
 we be in they . and then the whole scene , down to our final escape , 
 repeat itself , only not quite so violently . Mahomed 's skilful steering 
 and the air - tight compartment save our life . in five minute we be 
 through , and drift - for we be too exhausted to do anything to 
 help ourselves except keep her head straight - with the most startling 
 rapidity round the headland which I have describe . 

 round we go with the tide , until we get well under the lee of the 
 point , and then suddenly the speed slacken , we cease to make way , 
 and finally appear to be in dead water . the storm have entirely pass , 
 leave a clean - washed sky behind it ; the headland intercept the heavy 
 sea that have be occasion by the squall , and the tide , which have 
 be run so fiercely up the river   for we be now in the mouth of a 
 river , be sluggish before it turn , so we float quietly , and before 
 the moon go down manage to bail out the boat thoroughly and get she 
 a little ship - shape . Leo be sleep profoundly , and on the whole I 
 think it wise not to wake he . it be true he be sleep in wet 
 clothe , but the night be now so warm that I think   and so do Job 
 that they be not likely to injure a man of his unusually vigorous 
 constitution . besides , we have no dry one at hand . 

 presently the moon go down , and leave we float on the water , now 
 only heave like some troubled woman 's breast , with leisure to reflect 
 upon all that we have go through and all that we have escape . Job 
 station himself at the bow , Mahomed keep his post at the tiller , and I 
 sit on a seat in the middle of the boat close to where Leo be lie . 

 the moon go slowly down in chastened loveliness ; she depart like 
 some sweet bride into her chamber , and long veil - like shadow creep up 
 the sky through which the star peep shyly out . soon , however , they 
 too begin to pale before a splendour in the east , and then the quivering 
 footstep of the dawn come rush across the new - bear blue , and shake 
 the high star from their place . quieter and yet more quiet grow the 
 sea , quiet as the soft mist that brood on her bosom , and cover up 
 her troubling , as the illusive wreath of sleep brood upon a pain - rack 
 mind , cause it to forget its sorrow . from the east to the west 
 speed the angel of the Dawn , from sea to sea , from mountain - top to 
 mountain - top , scatter light with both their hand . on they speed out 
 of the darkness , perfect , glorious , like spirit of the just breaking 
 from the tomb ; on , over the quiet sea , over the low coastline , and the 
 swamp beyond , and the mountain above they ; over those who sleep in 
 peace and those who wake in sorrow ; over the evil and the good ; over the 
 living and the dead ; over the wide world and all that breathe or have 
 breathe thereon . 

 it be a wonderfully beautiful sight , and yet sad , perhaps , from the 
 very excess of its beauty . the arise sun ; the set sun ! there we 
 have the symbol and the type of humanity , and all thing with which 
 humanity have to do . the symbol and the type , yes , and the earthly 
 beginning , and the end also . and on that morning this come home to I 
 with a peculiar force . the sun that rise to - day for we have set last 
 night for eighteen of our fellow - voyager ! - have set everlastingly for 
 eighteen whom we know ! 

 the dhow have go down with they , they be toss about among the 
 rock and seaweed , so much human drift on the great ocean of Death ! and 
 we four be save . but one day a sunrise will come when we shall be 
 among those who be lose , and then other will watch those glorious 
 ray , and grow sad in the midst of beauty , and dream of death in the 
 full glow of arise life ! 

 for this be the lot of man .

 the head of the ETHIOPIAN 

 at length the herald and forerunner of the royal sun have do their

 VI 

 an early christian CEREMONY 

 next morning , at the early light of dawn , we rise , perform such 
 ablution as circumstance would allow , and generally make ready to 
 start . I be bind to say that when there be sufficient light to enable 
 we to see each other 's face I , for one , burst out into a roar of 
 laughter . Job 's fat and comfortable countenance be swell out to 
 nearly twice its natural size from mosquito bite , and Leo 's condition 
 be not much well . indeed , of the three I have come off much the good , 
 probably owe to the toughness of my dark skin , and to the fact that 
 a good deal of it be cover by hair , for since we have start from 
 England I have allow my naturally luxuriant beard to grow at its 
 own sweet will . but the other two be , comparatively speak , clean 
 shave , which of course give the enemy a large extent of open country 
 to operate on , though in Mahomed 's case the mosquito , recognise the 
 taste of a true believer , would not touch he at any price . how often , 
 I wonder , during the next week or so do we wish that we be flavour 
 like an Arab ! 

 by the time that we have do laugh as heartily as our swollen lip 
 would allow , it be daylight , and the morning breeze be come up from 
 the sea , cut lane through the dense marsh mist , and here and there 
 roll they before it in great ball of fleecy vapour . so we set 
 our sail , and have first take a look at the two dead lion and the 
 alligator , which we be of course unable to skin , be destitute of 
 mean of cure the pelt , we start , and , sail through the lagoon , 
 follow the course of the river on the farth side . at midday , when 
 the breeze drop , we be fortunate enough to find a convenient piece 
 of dry land on which to camp and light a fire , and here we cook two 
 wild - duck and some of the waterbuck 's flesh - not in a very appetising 
 way , it be true , but still sufficiently . the rest of the buck 's flesh 
 we cut into strip and hang in the sun to dry into " biltong , " as , I 
 believe , the south african Dutch call flesh thus prepare . on this 
 welcome patch of dry land we stop till the follow dawn , and , as 
 before , spend the night in warfare with the mosquito , but without 
 other trouble . the next day or two pass in similar fashion , and 
 without noticeable adventure , except that we shoot a speciman of a 
 peculiarly graceful hornless buck , and see many variety of water - lily 
 in full bloom , some of they blue and of exquisite beauty , though few 
 of the flower be perfect , owe to the prevalence of a white 
 water - maggot with a green head that feed upon they . 

 it be on the fifth day of our journey , when we have travel , so far 
 as we could reckon , about one hundred and thirty - five to a hundred and 
 forty mile westward from the coast , that the first event of any real 
 importance occur . on that morning the usual wind fail we about 
 eleven o'clock , and after pull a little way we be force to halt , 
 more or less exhausted , at what appear to be the junction of our 
 stream with another of a uniform width of about fifty foot . some tree 
 grow near at hand - the only tree in all this country be along the 
 bank of the river , and under these we rest , and then , the land be 
 fairly dry just here , walk a little way along the edge of the river to 
 prospect , and shoot a few waterfowl for food . before we have go fifty

 the whale - boat be at an end , for not two hundred yard above where 
 we have stop be a succession of shallow and mudbank , with not six 
 inch of water over they . it be a watery cul de sac . 

 turn back , we walk some way along the bank of the other river , and 
 soon come to the conclusion , from various indication , that it be not 
 a river at all , but an ancient canal , like the one which be to be see 
 above Mombasa , on the Zanzibar coast , connect the Tana River with 
 the Ozy , in such a way as to enable the shipping come down the Tana 
 to cross to the Ozy , and reach the sea by it , and thus avoid the very 
 dangerous bar that block the mouth of the Tana . the canal before we 
 have evidently be dig out by man at some remote period of the world 's 
 history , and the result of his digging still remain in the shape of 
 the raise bank that have no doubt once form towing - path . except here 
 and there , where they have be hollow out by the water or fall in , 
 these bank of stiff bind clay be at a uniform distance from each 
 other , and the depth of the stream also appear to be uniform . current

 the FEAST , and after !

 and then , without wait for an answer , he turn and walk to his 
 litter , and in ten minute from that time we be all well under way . 

 it take we an hour and more to cross the cup of the volcanic plain , 
 and another half - hour or so to climb the edge on the farth side . once

 which they now and again plunge into the ground before they , the reason

 with which I be not acquaint , so that place which might be safe 
 enough to cross one month would certainly swallow the wayfarer the next . 
 never do I see a more dreary and depressing scene . mile on mile of 
 quagmire , varied only by bright green strip of comparatively solid

 or enormous iguana , I do not know which , that feed , Billali tell I , upon 
 the waterfowl , also large quantity of a hideous black water - snake , of

 cobra 's or a puff adder 's . the bull - frog be also very large , and 
 with voice proportionate to their size ; and as for the mosquito - the

 on we go through it all , till at last the sun sink in sullen splendour

 Knowledge be to the strong , and we be weak . too much wisdom would

 above I , as I lay , shine the eternal star , and there at my foot the

 what would it be to cast off this earthy robe , to have do for ever

 these and many such thought pass through my mind that night . they

 then I fall to reflect upon the undertaking on which we be bent , 
 and what a wild one it be , and yet how strangely the story seem to

 give unende life ? could it be possible that any fluid or essence

 be power . he might give a lifetime to the study of each art or science . 
 well , if that be so , and this she be practically immortal , which 
 I do not for one moment believe , how be it that , with all these thing

 the PLAIN of K"R

 " SHE "

 she lift her white and rounded arm - never have I see such arm

 XIV 

 a SOUL in HELL 

 it be nearly ten o'clock at night when I cast myself down upon my bed , 
 and begin to gather my scattered wit , and reflect upon what I have see 
 and hear . but the more I reflect the less I could make of it . be I 
 mad , or drunk , or dream , or be I merely the victim of a gigantic 
 and most elaborate hoax ? how be it possible that I , a rational man , 
 not unacquainted with the lead scientific fact of our history , and 
 hitherto an absolute and utter disbeliever in all the hocus - pocus which 
 in Europe go by the name of the supernatural , could believe that I have 
 within the last few minute be engage in conversation with a woman 
 two thousand and odd year old ? the thing be contrary to the experience 
 of human nature , and absolutely and utterly impossible . it must be a 
 hoax , and yet , if it be a hoax , what be I to make of it ? what , too , 
 be to be say of the figure on the water , of the woman 's extraordinary 
 acquaintance with the remote past , and her ignorance , or apparent 
 ignorance , of any subsequent history ? what , too , of her wonderful and 
 awful loveliness ? this , at any rate , be a patent fact , and beyond the 
 experience of the world . no merely mortal woman could shine with such 
 a supernatural radiance . about that she have , at any rate , be in the 
 right - it be not safe for any man to look upon such beauty . I be 
 a harden vessel in such matter , have , with the exception of one 
 painful experience of my green and tender youth , put the soft sex 
  I sometimes think that this be a misnomer   almost entirely out of my 
 thought . but now , to my intense horror , I know that I could never put 
 away the vision of those glorious eye ; and alas ! the very diablerie 
 of the woman , whilst it horrify and repel , attract in even a 
 great degree . a person with the experience of two thousand year at 
 she back , with the command of such tremendous power , and the knowledge 
 of a mystery that could hold off death , be certainly worth fall 
 in love with , if ever woman be . but , alas ! it be not a question of 
 whether or no she be worth it , for so far as I could judge , not be 
 verse in such matter , I , a fellow of my college , note for what my 
 acquaintance be pleased to call my misogyny , and a respectable man 
 now well on in middle life , have fall absolutely and hopelessly in love 
 with this white sorceress . nonsense ; it must be nonsense ! she have warn 
 I fairly , and I have refuse to take the warning . curse on the fatal 
 curiosity that be ever prompt man to draw the veil from woman , 
 and curse on the natural impulse that beget it ! it be the cause of 
 half - ay , and more than half - of our misfortune . why can not man be 
 content to live alone and be happy , and let the woman live alone and be 
 happy too ? but perhaps they would not be happy , and I be not sure that 
 we should either . here be a nice state of affair . I , at my age , to fall 
 a victim to this modern Circe ! but then she be not modern , at least she 
 say not . she be almost as ancient as the original Circe . 

 I tear my hair , and jump up from my couch , feel that if I do 
 not do something I should go off my head . what do she mean about the 
 scarabæus too ? it be Leo 's scarabæus , and have come out of the old 
 coffer that Vincey have leave in my room nearly one - and - twenty year 
 before . could it be , after all , that the whole story be true , and 
 the writing on the sherd be not a forgery , or the invention of some 
 crack - brain , long - forget individual ? and if so , could it be that 
  Leo be the man that she be wait for - the dead man who be to be 
 bear again ! impossible ! the whole thing be gibberish ! who ever hear of 
 a man be bear again ? 

 but if it be possible that a woman could exist for two thousand year , 
 this might be possible also - anything might be possible . I myself might , 
 for aught I know , be a reincarnation of some other forget self , or 
 perhaps the last of a long line of ancestral self . well , vive la 
 guerre ! why not ? only , unfortunately , I have no recollection of these 
 previous condition . the idea be so absurd to I that I burst out 
 laughing , and , address the sculptured picture of a grim - look 
 warrior on the cave wall , call out to he aloud , " who know , old 
 fellow ? - perhaps I be your contemporary . by Jove ! perhaps I be you and 
 you be I , " and then I laugh again at my own folly , and the sound of 
 my laughter ring dismally along the vaulted roof , as though the ghost of 
 the warrior have echo the ghost of a laugh . 

 next I bethink I that I have not be to see how Leo be , so , take 
 up one of the lamp which be burn at my bedside , I slip off my 
 shoe and creep down the passage to the entrance of his sleep cave . 
 the draught of the night air be lift his curtain to and fro gently , 
 as though spirit hand be draw and redrawe it . I slide into the 
 vault - like apartment , and look round . there be a light by which I 
 could see that Leo be lie on the couch , toss restlessly in his 
 fever , but asleep . at his side , half - lie on the floor , half - lean

 beneath his eye , and his breath come heavily . he be very , very ill ;

 alone in the world . and yet if he live he would perhaps be my rival 
 with Ayesha ; even if he be not the man , what chance should I , 
 middle - aged and hideous , have against his bright youth and beauty ? well , 
 thank Heaven ! my sense of right be not dead . she have not kill that 
 yet ; and , as I stand there , I pray to Heaven in my heart that my boy , 
 my more than son , might live - ay , even if he prove to be the man . 

 then I go back as softly as I have come , but still I could not sleep ; 
 the sight and thought of dear Leo lie there so ill have but add fuel 
 to the fire of my unrest . my wearied body and overstrain mind awaken 
 all my imagination into preternatural activity . idea , vision , almost 
 inspiration , float before it with startling vividness . Most of they 
 be grotesque enough , some be ghastly , some recall thought and 
 sensation that have for year be bury in the débris of my past 
 life . but , behind and above they all , hover the shape of that awful 
 woman , and through they gleam the memory of her entrance loveliness . 
 up and down the cave I strode - up and down . 

 suddenly I observe , what I have not notice before , that there be a 
 narrow aperture in the rocky wall . I take up the lamp and examine it ; 
 the aperture lead to a passage . now , I be still sufficiently sensible

 be asleep . partly to see where it go to , and partly from a restless

 stair , which I descend ; the stair end in another passage , or rather 
 tunnel , also hew out of the bed - rock , and run , so far as I could 
 judge , exactly beneath the gallery that lead to the entrance of our 
 room , and across the great central cave . I go on down it : it be as 
 silent as the grave , but still , draw by some sensation or attraction

 yard of space , I come to another passage run at right angle , and 
 here an awful thing happen to I : the sharp draught catch my lamp

 mysterious place . I take a couple of stride forward so as to clear the 
 bisecting tunnel , be terribly afraid lest I should turn up it in 
 the dark if once I get confuse as to the direction , and then pause to 
 think . what be I to do ? I have no match ; it seem awful to attempt that 
 long journey back through the utter gloom , and yet I could not stand 
 there all night , and , if I do , probably it would not help I much , for 
 in the bowel of the rock it would be as dark at midday as at midnight . 
 I look back over my shoulder - not a sight or a sound . I peer forward 
 into the darkness : surely , far away , I see something like the faint glow 
 of fire . perhaps it be a cave where I could get a light - at any rate , 
 it be worth investigate . slowly and painfully I creep along the 
 tunnel , keep my hand against its wall , and feel at every step with 
 my foot before I put it down , fear lest I should fall into some 
 pit . thirty pace - there be a light , a broad light that come and go , 
 shin through curtain ! fifty pace - it be close at hand ! sixty - oh , 
 great heaven ! 

 I be at the curtain , and they do not hang close , so I could see 
 clearly into the little cavern beyond they . it have all the appearance of 
 be a tomb , and be light up by a fire that burn in its centre with a 
 whitish flame and without smoke . indeed , there , to the left , be a stone

 with something white throw over it . to the right be a similar shelf ,

 flickering flame . suddenly , as I be try to make up my mind what 
 to do , with a convulsive movement that somehow give an impression of

 it be she herself ! 

 she be clothe , as I have see she when she unveil , in the kirtle of 
 cling white , cut low upon her bosom , and bind in at the waist with 
 the barbaric double - headed snake , and , as before , her ripple black 
 hair fall in heavy mass down her back . but her face be what catch my 
 eye , and hold I as in a vice , not this time by the force of its beauty ,

 indeed , but the agony , the blind passion , and the awful vindictiveness 
 display upon those quivering feature , and in the tortured look of the 
 upturned eye , be such as surpass my power of description . 

 for a moment she stand still , her hand raise high above her head , and 
 as she do so the white robe slip from she down to her golden girdle , 
 bar the blind loveliness of her form . she stand there , her finger 
 clench , and the awful look of malevolence gather and deepen on her

 suddenly I think of what would happen if she discover I , and the 
 reflection make I turn sick and faint . but , even if I have know that I

 Down come the clench hand to her side , then up again above her head , 
 and , as I be a living and honourable man , the white flame of the fire

 and every scroll and detail of the rockwork . 

 Down come the ivory arm again , and as they do so she speak , or rather 
 hiss , in Arabic , in a note that curdle my blood , and for a second 
 stop my heart . 

 " curse she , may she be everlastingly accurse . " 

 the arm fall and the flame sink . up they go again , and the broad 
 tongue of fire shoot up after they ; and then again they fall . 

 " curse her memory - accurse be the memory of the Egyptian . " 

 up again , and again down . 

 " curse she , the daughter of the Nile , because of her beauty . 

 " curse she , because her magic hath prevail against I . 

 " curse she , because she hold my beloved from I . " 

 and again the flame dwindle and shrank . 

 she put her hand before her eye , and abandon the hiss tone , 
 cry aloud : - 

 " what be the use of cursing ? - she prevail , and she be go . " 

 then she recommence with an even more frightful energy : - 

 " curse she where she be . let my curse reach she where she be and 
 disturb her rest . 

 " curse she through the starry space . let her shadow be accurse . 

 " let my power find she even there . 

 " let she hear I even there . let she hide herself in the blackness . 

 " let she go down into the pit of despair , because I shall one day find 
 she . " 

 again the flame fall , and again she cover her eye with her hand . 

 " it be of no use - no use , " she wail ; " who can reach those who sleep ? 
 not even I can reach they . " 

 then once more she begin her unholy rite . 

 " curse she when she shall be bear again . let she be bear accurse . 

 " let she be utterly accuse from the hour of her birth until sleep find 
 she . 

 " Yea , then , let she be accurse ; for then shall I overtake she with my 
 vengeance , and utterly destroy she . " 

 and so on . the flame rise and fall , reflect itself in her agonised 
 eye ; the hiss sound of her terrible malediction , and no word of 
 mine can convey how terrible they be , run round the wall and die 
 away in little echo , and the fierce light and deep gloom alternate 
 themselves on the white and dreadful form stretch upon that bi of 
 stone . 

 but at length she seem to wear herself out and cease . she sit herself 
 down upon the rocky floor , shake the dense cloud of her beautiful hair 
 over her face and breast , and begin to sob terribly in the torture of a 
 heartrende despair . 

 " two thousand year , " she moan - " two thousand year have I want and 
 endure ; but though century doth still creep on to century , and time 
 give place to time , the sting of memory hath not lessen , the light of 
 hope doth not shine more bright . oh ! to have live two thousand year , 
 with all my passion eat out my heart , and with my sin ever before I . 
 oh , that for I life can not bring forgetfulness ! oh , for the weary year 
 that have be and be yet to come , and evermore to come , endless and 
 without end ! 

 " my love ! my love ! my love ! why do that stranger bring thee back to I 
 after this sort ? for five hundred year I have not suffer thus . oh , 
 if I sin against thee , have I not wipe away the sin ? when wilt thou 
 come back to I who have all , and yet without thee have naught ? what be 
 there that I can do ? what ? what ? what ? and perchance she - perchance that

 why could I not die with thee , I who slay thee ? alas , that I can not die ! 
 alas ! alas ! " and she fling herself prone upon the ground , and sob and 
 weep till I think her heart must burst . 

 suddenly she cease , raise herself to her foot , rearrange her robe , 
 and , toss back her long lock impatiently , sweep across to where the 
 figure lie upon the stone . 

 " oh Kallikrates , " she cry , and I tremble at the name , " I must look 
 upon thy face again , though it be agony . it be a generation since

 tremble finger she seize the corner of the sheet - like wrapping that 
 cover the form upon the stone bier , and then pause . when she speak 
 again , it be in a kind of awed whisper , as though her idea be 
 terrible even to herself . 

 " shall I raise thee , " she say , apparently address the corpse , ' so 
 that thou standest there before I , as of old ? I can do it , " and she 
 hold out her hand over the sheeted dead , while her whole frame become 
 rigid and terrible to see , and her eye grow fix and dull . I shrink in 
 horror behind the curtain , my hair stand up upon my head , and , whether 
 it be my imagination or a fact I be unable to say , but I think that

 sheet to lift as though it lie on the breast of one who sleep . suddenly

 " to what purpose ? " she say gloomily . " of what good be it to recall the 
 semblance of life when I can not recall the spirit ? even if thou stoodest 
 before I thou wouldst not know I , and couldst but do what I bid thee . 
 the life in thee would be my life , and not thy life , Kallikrates . " 

 for a moment she stand there brooding , and then cast herself down on her 
 knee beside the form , and begin to press her lip against the sheet , 
 and weep . there be something so horrible about the sight of this 
 awe - inspire woman let loose her passion on the dead - so much more 
 horrible even than anything that have go before - that I could no long 
 bear to look at it , and , turning , begin to creep , shake as I be in 
 every limb , slowly along the pitch - dark passage , feel in my trembling

 on I stumble , I scarcely know how . twice I fall , once I turn up the 
 bisecting passage , but fortunately find out my mistake in time . for

 when I come to I notice a faint ray of light in the passage just behind

 XV 

 ayesha GIVES judgment 

 the next thing that I remember be open my eye and perceive the 
 form of Job , who have now practically recover from his attack of fever . 
 he be stand in the ray of light that pierce into the cave from 
 the outer air , shake out my clothe as a makeshift for brush they , 
 which he could not do because there be no brush , and then fold they 
 up neatly and lay they on the foot of the stone couch . this do , he 
 get my travel dressing - case out of the Gladstone bag , and open it

      " the cave of torture . " I afterwards see this dreadful

 she cease , and a faint murmur of horror run round the cave . as for the

 the tombs of K"R 

 after the prisoner have be remove Ayesha wave her hand , and the

 " in the year four thousand two hundred and fifty - nine from the founding 
 of the City of imperial K"r be this cave   or burial place   complete

      this phrase be remarkable , as seem to indicate a 
  belief in a future state . - Editor . 

 " Thou se , oh Holly , " she say , " this people found the city , of 
 which the ruin yet cumber the plain yonder , four thousand year before 
 this cave be finish . yet , when first mine eye beheld it two thousand 
 year ago , be it even as it be now . Judge , therefore , how old must that

 " I , Junis , a priest of the Great Temple of K"r , write this upon the 
 rock of the burying - place in the year four thousand eight hundred and 
 three from the founding of K"r . K"r be fall ! no more shall the 
 mighty feast in her hall , no more shall she rule the world , and her 
 navy go out to commerce with the world . K"r be fall ! and her mighty 
 work and all the city of K"r , and all the harbour that she build 
 and the canal that she make , be for the wolf and the owl and the wild 
 swan , and the barbarian who come after . twenty and five moon ago do 
 a cloud settle upon K"r , and the hundred city of K"r , and out of the 
 cloud come a pestilence that slay her people , old and young , one 
 with another , and spar not . one with another they turn black and 
 die - the young and the old , the rich and the poor , the man and the 
 woman , the prince and the slave . the pestilence slew and slew , and 
 cease not by day or by night , and those who escape from the pestilence

 K"r be preserve accord to the ancient rite , because of the number

 the cave , through the hole in the floor of the cave . then , at last , a

 down to the coast and take ship and sail northward ; and now be I , the 
 Priest Junis , who write this , the last man leave alive of this great city 
 of man , but whether there be any yet leave in the other city I know 
 not . this do I write in misery of heart before I die , because K"r 
 the Imperial be no more , and because there be none to worship in her 
 temple , and all her palace be empty , and her prince and her captain 
 and her trader and her fair woman have pass off the face of the 
 earth . " 

 I give a sigh of astonishment - the utter desolation depict in this 
 rude scrawl be so overpowering . it be terrible to think of this 
 solitary survivor of a mighty people record its fate before he too 
 go down into darkness . what must the old man have feel as , in ghastly

 little space of gloom , he in a few brief line daub the history of his 
 nation 's death upon the cavern wall ? what a subject for the moralist , or 
 the painter , or indeed for any one who can think ! 

 " Doth it not occur to thee , oh Holly , " say Ayesha , lay her hand upon 
 my shoulder , " that those man who sail North may have be the father 
 of the first Egyptians ? " 

 " Nay , I know not , " I say ; " it seem that the world be very old . " 

 " Old ? yes , it be old indeed . time after time have nation , ay , and rich 
 and strong nation , learn in the art , be and pass away and 
 be forget , so that no memory of they remain . this be but one of 
 several ; for Time eat up the work of man , unless , indeed , he dig in 
 cave like the people of K"r , and then mayhap the sea swallow they , or 
 the earthquake shake they in . who know what hath be on the earth , or 
 what shall be ? there be no new thing under the sun , as the wise Hebrew 
 write long ago . yet be not these people utterly destroy , as I think . 
 some few remain in the other city , for their city be many . but 
 the barbarian from the south , or perchance my people , the Arabs , 
 come down upon they , and take their woman to wife , and the race of the 
 Amahagger that be now be a bastard brood of the mighty son of K"r , and 
 behold it dwelleth in the tomb with its father ' bone .     but I know 
 not : who can know ? my art can not pierce so far into the blackness of 
 Time 's night . a great people be they . they conquer till none be 
 leave to conquer , and then they dwelt at ease within their rocky mountain 
 wall , with their man servant and their maid servant , their minstrel , 
 their sculptor , and their concubine , and trade and quarrel , and 
 eat and hunt and sleep and make merry till their time come . but come , 
 I will show thee the great pit beneath the cave whereof the writing 
 speak . never shall thine eye witness such another sight . " 

      the name of the race Ama - hagger would seem to indicate a 
  curious mingling of race such as might easily have occur 
  in the neighbourhood of the Zambesi . the prefix " Ama " be 
  common to the Zulu and kindre race , and signify 
  " people , " while " hagger " be an arabic word mean a stone . 
  - Editor . 

 accordingly I follow she to a side passage opening out of the main 
 cave , then down a great number of step , and along an underground shaft 
 which can not have be less than sixty foot beneath the surface of the

 " come , " I say , " I have see enough . these be the body of those who 
 die of the great sickness , be it not so ? " I add , as we turn away . 

 " Yea . the people of K"r ever embalm their dead , as do the Egyptians ,

 there be no material to turn to dust . about the body on the stone

      all the linen that the Amahagger wear be take from the
