 degradation to which he have sink . on the contrary , his well nature 
 rise up in arm against his fallen self , as I see clearly enough later 
 on . 

 Ayesha laugh again , and then quickly veil herself , and make a sign 
 to the girl mute , who have be watch the whole scene with curious 
 startled eye . the girl leave , and presently return , follow by two 
 male mute , to whom the Queen make another sign . Thereon they all three 
 seize the body of poor Ustane by the arm , and drag it heavily down 
 the cavern and away through the curtain at the end . Leo watch it for 
 a little while , and then cover his eye with his hand , and it too , to 
 my excited fancy , seem to watch we as it go . 

 " there pass the dead past , " say Ayesha , solemnly , as the curtain 
 shake and fall back into their place , when the ghastly procession 
 have vanish behind they . and then , with one of those extraordinary 
 transition of which I have already speak , she again throw off her 
 veil , and break out , after the ancient and poetic fashion of the 
 dweller in Arabia ,     into a pæan of triumph or epithalamium , which , 
 wild and beautiful as it be , be exceedingly difficult to render into 
 English , and ought by right to be sing to the music of a cantata , 
 rather than write and read . it be divide into two part - one 
 descriptive or definitive , and the other personal ; and , as nearly as I 
 can remember , run as follow : - 

 Love be like a flower in the desert . 

 it be like the aloe of Arabia that bloom but once and die ; it bloom 
 in the salt emptiness of life , and the brightness of its beauty be set 
 upon the waste as a star be set upon a storm . 

 it hath the sun above that be the Spirit , and above it blow the air of 
 its divinity . 

 at the echoing of a step , Love bloom , I say ; I say Love bloom , and 
 bend her beauty down to he who passeth by . 

 he plucketh it , yea , he plucketh the red cup that be full of honey , 
 and beareth it away ; away across the desert , away till the flower be 
 wither , away till the desert be do . 

 there be only one perfect flower in the wilderness of life . 

 that flower be Love ! 

 there be only one fix star in the midst of our wandering . 

 that star be Love ! 

 there be only one hope in our despairing night . 

 that hope be Love ! 

 all else be false . all else be shadow move upon water . all else be 
 wind and vanity . 

 who shall say what be the weight or the measure of love ? 

 it be bear of the flesh , it dwelleth in the spirit . from each doth it 
 draw its comfort . 

 for beauty it be as a star . 

 many be its shape , but all be beautiful , and none know where the star 
 rise , or the horizon where it shall set . 

      among the ancient Arabians the power of poetic 
  declamation , either in verse or prose , be hold in the 
  high honour and esteem , and he who excel in it be 
  know as " Khâteb , " or orator . every year a general assembly 
  be hold at which the rival poet repeat their 
  composition , when those poem which be judge to be the 
  good be , so soon as the knowledge and the art of writing 
  become general , inscribe on silk in letter of gold , and 
  publicly exhibit , be know as " Al Modhahabât , " or 
  golden verse . in the poem give above by Mr. Holly , Ayesha 
  evidently follow the traditional poetic manner of her 
  people , which be to embody their thought in a series of 
  somewhat disconnect sentence , each remarkable for its 
  beauty and the grace of its expression . - Editor . 

 then , turn to Leo , and lay her hand upon his shoulder , she go 
 on in a full and more triumphant tone , speak in balanced sentence 
 that gradually grow and swell from idealised prose into pure and 
 majestic verse : - 

 long have I love thee , oh , my love ; yet have my love not lessen . 

 long have I wait for thee , and behold my reward be at hand - be here ! 

 far away I see thee once , and thou wast take from I . 

 then in a grave sow I the seed of patience , and shine upon it with the 
 sun of hope , and water it with tear of repentance , and breathe on

 bear fruit . Lo ! out of the grave hath it spring . yea , from among the 
 dry bone and ash of the dead . 

 I have wait and my reward be with I . 

 I have overcome death , and death bring back to I he that be dead . 

 therefore do I rejoice , for fair be the future . 

 Green be the path that we shall tread across the everlaste meadow . 

 the hour be at hand . Night hath flee away into the valley . 

 the dawn kisseth the mountain top . 

 Soft shall we live , my love , and easy shall we go . 

 crown shall we be with the diadem of king . 

 worship and wonder strike all people of the world , Blinded shall 
 fall before our beauty and might . 

 from time unto time shall our greatness thunder on , roll like a 
 chariot through the dust of endless day . 

 laugh shall we speed in our victory and pomp , laugh like the 
 Daylight as he leap along the hill . 

 onward , still triumphant to a triumph ever new ! 

 onward , in our power to a power unattaine ! 

 onward , never weary , clothe with splendour for a robe ! 

 till accomplished be our fate , and the night be rush down . 

 she pause in her strange and most thrill allegorical chant , of

 " perchance thou dost not believe my word , Kallikrates - perchance thou

 she pause awhile and then continue , " but stay , if thy heart be yet

 without stop to think - indeed , speak for myself , I have almost

 the dead and live MEET

 " Behold now , let the dead and living meet ! across the gulf of Time they

 " ay , the sleep shall roll away , and the voice shall be hear , when down

 " therefore , have no fear , Kallikrates , when thou - living , and but lately

 " Behold ! "

 " Behold ! I have prepare against this happy hour ! " and go to the

      after some month of consideration of this statement I 
  be bind to confess that I be not quite satisfied of its 
  truth . it be perfectly true that Ayesha commit a murder ,

  old one , for he be without that experience of the order of 
  thing that in certain thoughtful disposition can hardly 
  fail to produce cynicism , and that disregard of acknowledge 
  method and establish custom which we call evil . now the 
  old man upon the earth be but a babe compare to Ayesha ,

  thing worth live for , and that be love in its high

  may be think of they , she have some virtue develop to a

  instance . - L. H. H.

 JOB have a PRESENTIMENT

      I regret to say that I be never able to ascertain if 
  she be invulnerable against the ordinary accident of

  impulse without some valid object . - L. H. H. 

 the whole thing sound like a dream or some extraordinary invention of

 XXIII 

 the TEMPLE of truth 

 our preparation do not take we very long . we put a change of clothing 
 apiece and some spare boot into my Gladstone bag , also we take our 
 revolver and an express rifle each , together with a good supply of 
 ammunition , a precaution to which , under Providence , we subsequently 
 owe our life over and over again . the rest of our gear , together with 
 our heavy rifle , we leave behind we . 

 a few minute before the appoint time we once more attend in 
 Ayesha 's boudoir , and find she also ready , her dark cloak throw over 
 her winding - sheetlike wrapping . 

 " be ye prepared for the great venture ? " she say . 

 " we be , " I answer , " though for my part , Ayesha , I have no faith in 
 it . " 

 " ah , my Holly , " she say , " thou art of a truth like those old Jews - of 
 whom the memory vex I so sorely - unbelieving , and hard to accept 
 that which they have not know . but thou shalt see ; for unless my mirror 
 beyond lie , " and she point to the font of crystal water , " the path be 
 yet open as it be of old time . and now let we start upon the new life 
 which shall end - who knoweth where ? " 

 " ah , " I echo , " who knoweth where ? " and we pass down into the great 
 central cave , and out into the light of day . at the mouth of the cave we

 with they I be relieve to see our old friend Billali , for whom I 
 have conceive a sort of affection . it appear that , for reason not 
 necessary to explain at length , Ayesha have think it well that , with

 which , however suitable they might be for sarcophagi - a singularly

 certainly do not consume the body give to their keeping - be

 a soul be to be see , and consequently I do not believe that our 
 departure be know to anybody , except perhaps the mute who wait on 
  she , and they be , of course , in the habit of keep what they see 
 to themselves . 

 in a few minute ' time we be step out sharply across the great 
 cultivate plain or lake bed , frame like a vast emerald in its setting 
 of frown cliff , and have another opportunity of wonder at the 
 extraordinary nature of the site choose by these old people of K"r for 
 their capital , and at the marvellous amount of labour , ingenuity , and 
 engineering skill that must have be bring into requisition by the 
 founder of the city to drain so huge a sheet of water , and to keep 
 it clear of subsequent accumulation . it be , indeed , so far as my 
 experience go , an unequalled instance of what man can do in the face 
 of nature , for in my opinion such achievement as the Suez Canal or 
 even the Mont Cenis Tunnel do not approach this ancient undertaking in 
 magnitude and grandeur of conception . 

 when we have be walk for about half an hour , enjoy ourselves 
 exceedingly in the delightful cool which about this time of the day 
 always appear to descend upon the great plain of K"r , and which in 
 some degree atone for the want of any land or sea breeze - for all wind 
 be keep off by the rocky mountain wall - we begin to get a clear view of 
 what Billali have inform we be the ruin of the great city . and even 
 from that distance we could see how wonderful those ruin be , a fact 
 which with every step we take become more evident . the town be not 
 very large if compare to Babylon or Thebes , or other city of remote 
 antiquity ; perhaps its outer wall contain some twelve square mile of 
 ground , or a little more . nor have the wall , so far as we could judge 
 when we reach they , be very high , probably not more than forty foot , 
 which be about their present height where they have not through the 
 sinking of the ground , or some such cause , fall into ruin . the reason 
 of this , no doubt , be that the people of K"r , be protect from any 
 outside attack by far more tremendous rampart than any that the hand of 
 man could rear , only require they for show and to guard against civil 
 discord . but on the other hand they be as broad as they be high , 
 build entirely of dress stone , hewn , no doubt , from the vast cave , 
 and surround by a great moat about sixty foot in width , some reach 
 of which be still fill with water . about ten minute before the 
 sun finally sink we reach this moat , and pass down and through it , 
 clamber across what evidently be the pile - up fragment of a great 
 bridge in order to do so , and then with some little difficulty over the 
 slope of the wall to its summit . I wish that it lie within the power of 
 my pen to give some idea of the grandeur of the sight that then meet our 
 view . there , all bath in the red glow of the sink sun , be mile 
 upon mile of ruin - column , temple , shrine , and the palace of 
 king , vary with patch of green bush . of course , the roof of these 
 building have long since fall into decay and vanish , but owe to 
 the extreme massiveness of the style of building , and to the hardness 
 and durability of the rock employ , most of the party wall and great 
 column still remain stand .   

      in connection with the extraordinary state of 
  preservation of these ruin after so vast a lapse of time - 
  at least six thousand year - it must be remember that K"r 
  be not burn or destroy by an enemy or an earthquake , but 
  desert , owe to the action of a terrible plague . 
  consequently the house be leave unharmed ; also the climate 
  of the plain be remarkably fine and dry , and there be very 
  little rain or wind ; as a result of which these relic have 
  only to contend against the unaided action of time , that 
  work but slowly upon such massive block of masonry . - L. 
  H. H. 

 Straight before we stretch away what have evidently be the main 
 thoroughfare of the city , for it be very wide , wide than the Thames 
 Embankment , and regular , be , as we afterwards discover , pave , 
 or rather build , throughout of block of dress stone , such as be 
 employ in the wall , it be but little overgrown even now with grass 
 and shrub that could get no depth of soil to live in . what have be the 
 park and garden , on the contrary , be now dense jungle . indeed , it 
 be easy even from a distance to trace the course of the various road 
 by the burn - up appearance of the scanty grass that grow upon they . on 
 either side of this great thoroughfare be vast block of ruin , each 
 block , generally speak , be separate from its neighbour by a space 
 of what have once , I suppose , be garden - ground , but be now dense and 
 tangle bush . they be all build of the same coloured stone , and most 
 of they have pillar , which be as much as we could make out in the 
 fading light as we pass swiftly up the main road , that I believe I be 
 right in say no live foot have press for thousand of year .   

      Billali tell I that the Amahagger believe that the site 
  of the city be haunt , and could not be persuade to enter 
  it upon any consideration . indeed , I could see that he 
  himself do not at all like do so , and be only console 
  by the reflection that he be under the direct protection of 
  she . it strike Leo and myself as very curious that a 
  people which have no objection to live amongst the dead , 
  with whom their familiarity have perhaps breed contempt , and 
  even use their body for purpose of fuel , should be 
  terrify at approach the habitation that these very 
  depart have occupy when alive . after all , however , it be 
  only a savage inconsistency . - L. H. H. 

 presently we come to an enormous pile , which we rightly take to be a 
 temple cover at least eight acre of ground , and apparently arrange 
 in a series of court , each one enclose another of small size , on 
 the principle of a chinese nest of box , the court be separate one 
 from the other by row of huge column . and , while I think of it , I may 
 as well state a remarkable thing about the shape of these column , which 
 resemble none that I have ever see or hear of , be fashion with a 
 kind of waist at the centre , and swell out above and below . at first 
 we think that this shape be mean to roughly symbolise or suggest 
 the female form , as be a common habit amongst the ancient religious 
 architect of many creed . on the follow day , however , as we go up 
 the slope of the mountain , we discover a large quantity of the most 
 stately look palm , of which the truck grow exactly in this shape , 
 and I have now no doubt but that the first designer of those column 
 draw his inspiration from the graceful bend of those very palm , or 
 rather of their ancestor , which then , some eight or ten thousand year 
 ago , as now , beautify the slope of the mountain that have once form 
 the shore of the volcanic lake . 

 at the façade of this huge temple , which , I should imagine , be almost 
 as large as that of El - Karnac , at Thebes , some of the large column , 
 which I measure , be between eighteen to twenty foot in diameter at 
 the base , by about seventy foot in height , our little procession be

 " there be a spot here , kallikrate , " she say to Leo , who have run up to 
 help she down , " where one might sleep . two thousand year ago do thou 
 and I and that egyptian asp rest therein , but since then have I not set 
 foot here , nor any man , and perchance it have fall , " and , follow by 
 the rest of we , she pass up a vast flight of broken and ruin step 
 into the outer court , and look round into the gloom . presently she

 the spirit of life

 and then pass into the air , and the thought flash through my brain 
 that I be lose . but no ! in another instant my foot strike against a 
 rocky floor , and I feel that I be stand upon something solid , and 
 out of reach of the wind , which I could hear sing away overhead . as 
 I stand there thank Heaven for these small mercy , there be a slip 
 and a scuffle , and down come Leo alongside of I . 

 " Hulloa , old fellow ! " he call out , " be you there ? this be get 
 interesting , be it not ? " 

 just then , with a terrific yell , Job arrive right on the top of we , 
 knock we both down . by the time we have struggle to our foot again 
 Ayesha be stand among we , and bid we light the lamp , which 
 fortunately remain uninjured , as also do the spare jar of oil . 

 I get out my box of wax match , and they strike as merrily , there , in 
 that awful place , as they could have do in a London drawing - room . 

 in a couple of minute both the lamp be alight and reveal a curious 
 scene . we be huddle together in a rocky chamber , some ten foot 
 square , and scar enough we look ; that be , except Ayesha , who be 
 stand calmly with her arm fold , and wait for the lamp to burn 
 up . the chamber appear to be partly natural , and partly hollow out 
 of the top of the cone . the roof of the natural part be form of the 
 swing stone , and that of the back part of the chamber , which slop 
 downward , be hew from the live rock . for the rest , the place be warm 
 and dry - a perfect haven of rest compare to the giddy pinnacle above , 
 and the quivering spur that shoot out to meet it in mid - air . 

 " so ! " say she , ' safely have we come , though once I fear that 
 the rock stone would fall with you , and precipitate you into the 
 bottomless depth beneath , for I do believe that the cleft goeth down 
 to the very womb of the world . the rock whereon the stone resteth hath 
 crumble beneath the swing weight . and now that he , " nod towards 
 Job , who be sit on the floor , feebly wipe his forehead with a red 
 cotton pocket - handkerchief , " whom they rightly call the ' Pig , ' for as a 
 pig be he stupid , hath let fall the plank , it will not be easy to return 
 across the gulf , and to that end must I make a plan . but now rest a 
 while , and look upon this place . what think ye that it be ? " 

 " we know not , " I answer . 

 " wouldst thou believe , oh Holly , that once a man do choose this airy 
 nest for a daily habitation , and do here endure for many year ; leave 
 it only but one day in every twelve to seek food and water and oil that 
 the people bring , more than he could carry , and lay as an offering in 
 the mouth of the tunnel through which we pass hither ? " 

 we look up wonderingly , and she continue - 

 " yet so it be . there be a man - Noot , he name himself - who , though 
 he live in the latter day , have of the wisdom of the son of K"r . a 
 hermit be he , and a philosopher , and greatly skilled in the secret 
 of Nature , and he it be who discover the fire that I shall show you , 
 which be Nature 's blood and life , and also that he who bath therein , 
 and breathe thereof , should live while nature live . but like unto 
 thee , oh Holly , this man , Noot , would not turn his knowledge to account . 
 ' Ill , ' he say , ' be it for man to live , for man be bear to die . ' 
 therefore do he tell his secret to none , and therefore do he come and 
 live here , where the seeker after Life must pass , and be revere of 
 the Amahagger of the day as holy , and a hermit . and when first I come to 
 this country - know thou how I come , Kallikrates ? another time I will 
 tell thee , for it be a strange tale - I hear of this philosopher , and 
 wait for he when he come to fetch his food , and return with he 
 hither , though greatly do I fear to tread the gulf . then do I beguile 
 he with my beauty and my wit , and flatter he with my tongue , so that 
 he lead I down and show I the fire , and tell I the secret of the 
 Fire , but he would not suffer I to step therein , and , fear lest he 
 should slay I , I refrain , know that the man be very old , and soon 
 would die . and I return , have learn from he all that he know of 
 the wonderful Spirit of the World , and that be much , for the man 
 be wise and very ancient , and by purity and abstinence , and the 
 contemplation of his innocent mind , have wear thin the veil between that 
 which we see and the great invisible truth , the whisper of whose wing 
 at time we hear as they sweep through the gross air of the world . 
 then - it be but a very few day after , I meet thee , my Kallikrates , 
 who hadst wander hither with the beautiful Egyptian Amenartas , and I 
 learn to love for the first and last time , once and for ever , so that 
 it enter into my mind to come hither with thee , and receive the gift 
 of Life for thee and I . therefore come we , with that Egyptian who would 
 not be leave behind , and , behold , we find the old man Noot lie but 
 newly dead . there he lay , and his white beard cover he like a 
 garment , " and she point to a spot near where I be sit ; " but 
 surely he hath long since crumble into dust , and the wind hath bear 
 his ash hence . " 

 here I put out my hand and feel in the dust , and presently my finger 
 touch something . it be a human tooth , very yellow , but sound . I hold 
 it up and show it to Ayesha , who laugh . 

 " yes , " she say , " it be his without a doubt . behold what remaineth of 
 Noot , and the wisdom of Noot - one little tooth ! and yet that man have all 
 life at his command , and for his conscience ' sake would have none of 
 it . well , he lie there newly dead , and we descend whither I shall lead 
 you , and then , gather up all my courage , and court death that 
 I might perchance win so glorious a crown of life , I step into the 
 flame , and behold ! life such as ye can never know until ye feel it 
 also , flow into I , and I come forth undye , and lovely beyond 
 imagining . then do I stretch out mine arm to thee , Kallikrates , 
 and bid thee take thine immortal bride , and behold , as I speak , thou , 
 blind by my beauty , didst turn from I , and throw thine arm about the 
 neck of Amenartas . and then a great fury fill I , and make I mad , 
 and I seize the javelin that thou didst bear , and stab thee , so that 
 there , at my very foot , in the place of life , thou didst groan and go 
 down into death . I know not then that I have strength to slay with mine 
 eye and by the power of my will , therefore in my madness slew I with 
 the javelin .   

      it will be observe that Ayesha 's account of the death 
  of Kallikrates differ materially from that write on the 
  potsherd by Amenartas . the writing on the sherd say , " then 
  in her rage do she smite he by her magic , and he die . " 
  we never ascertain which be the correct version , but it 
  will be remember that the body of Kallikrates have a spear- 
  wound in the breast , which seem conclusive , unless , indeed , 
  it be inflict after death . another thing that we never 
  ascertain be how the two woman - she and the Egyptian 
  Amenartas - be able to bear the corpse of the man they both 
  love across the dread gulf and along the shake spur . what 
  a spectacle the two distracted creature must have present 
  in their grief and loveliness as they toil along that 
  awful place with the dead man between they ! probably however 
  the passage be easy then . - L. H. H. 

 " and when thou wast dead , ah ! I weep , because I be undying and thou 
 wast dead . I weep there in the place of life so that have I be mortal 
 any more my heart have surely break . and she , the swart Egyptian - she 
 curse I by her god . by Osiris do she curse I and by isis , by 
 Nephthys and by Anubis , by Sekhet , the cat - head , and by Set , call 
 down evil on I , evil and everlasting desolation . ah ! I can see her dark 
 face now lower o'er I like a storm , but she could not hurt I , and 
 I - I know not if I could hurt she . I do not try ; it be naught to I 
 then ; so together we bear thee hence . and afterwards I send she - the 
 Egyptian - away through the swamp , and it seem that she live to bear 
 a son and to write the tale that should lead thee , her husband , back to 
 I , her rival and thy murderess . 

 " such be the tale , my love , and now be the hour at hand that shall set 
 a crown upon it . like all thing on the earth , it be compound of evil 
 and of good - more of evil than of good , perchance ; and writ in letter 
 of blood . it be the truth ; naught have I hide from thee , Kallikrates . 
 and now one thing before the final moment of thy trial . we go down 
 into the presence of death , for Life and death be very near together , 
 and - who knoweth ? - that might happen which should separate we for 
 another space of wait . I be but a woman , and no prophetess , and I 
 can not read the future . but this I know - for I learn it from the 
 lip of the wise man Noot - that my life be but prolong and make more 
 bright . it can not live for aye . therefore , before we go , tell I , oh 
 Kallikrates , that of a truth thou dost forgive I , and dost love I from 
 thy heart . see , Kallikrates : much evil have I do - perchance it be 
 evil but two night ago to strike that girl who love thee cold in 
 death - but she disobey I and anger I , prophesy misfortune to 
 I , and I smote . be careful when power come to thee also , lest thou 
 too shouldst smite in thine anger or thy jealousy , for unconquerable 
 strength be a sore weapon in the hand of err man . yea , I have 
 sin - out of the bitterness bear of a great love have I sin - but 
 yet do I know the good from the evil , nor be my heart altogether 
 harden . Thy love , Kallikrates , shall be the gate of my redemption , 
 even as aforetime my passion be the path down which I run to evil . for 
 deep love unsatisfie be the hell of noble heart and a portion of the 
 accursed , but love that be mirror back more perfect from the soul of 
 our desire doth fashion wing to lift we above ourselves , and make we 
 what we might be . therefore , Kallikrates , take I by the hand , and lift 
 my veil with no more fear than though I be some peasant girl , and not 
 the wise and most beauteous woman in this wide world , and look I in 
 the eye , and tell I that thou dost forgive I with all thine heart , 
 and that will all thine heart thou dost worship I . " 

 she pause , and the strange tenderness in her voice seem to hover 
 round we like a memory . I know that the sound of it move I more even 
 than her word , it be so very human - so very womanly . Leo , too , be 
 strangely touch . Hitherto he have be fascinate against his well 
 judgment , something as a bird be fascinate by a snake , but now I think 
 that all this pass away , and he realise that he really love this 
 strange and glorious creature , as , alas ! I love she also . at any rate , 
 I see his eye fill with tear , and he step swiftly to she and undo 
 the gauzy veil , and then take she by the hand , and , gaze into her deep 
 eye , say aloud - 

 " Ayesha , I love thee with all my heart , and so far as forgiveness be 
 possible I forgive thee the death of Ustane . for the rest , it be between 
 thee and thy Maker ; I know naught of it . I only know that I love thee as 
 I never love before , and that I will cleave to thee to the end . " 

 " now , " answer Ayesha , with proud humility - " now when my lord doth 
 speak thus royally and give with so free a hand , it can not become I to 
 lag behind in word , and be beggar of my generosity . Behold ! " and she 
 take his hand and place it upon her shapely head , and then bent herself 
 slowly down till one knee for an instant touch the ground - " Behold ! in 
 token of submission do I bow I to my lord ! Behold ! " and she kiss he 
 on the lip , " in token of my wifely love do I kiss my lord . Behold ! " 
 and she lay her hand upon his heart , " by the sin I sin , by my lonely 
 century of wait wherewith it be wipe out , by the great love 
 wherewith I love , and by the Spirit - the Eternal Thing that doth beget 
 all life , from whom it ebb , to whom it doth return again - I swear : - 

 " I swear , even in this most holy hour of complete Womanhood , that I 
 will abandon evil and cherish Good . I swear that I will be ever guide 
 by thy voice in the straight path of Duty . I swear that I will eschew 
 Ambition , and through all my length of endless day set Wisdom over I 
 as a guide star to lead I unto Truth and a knowledge of the right . 
 I swear also that I will honour and will cherish thee , Kallikrates , who 
 hast be sweep by the wave of time back into my arm , ay , till the very 
 end , come it soon or late . I swear - nay , I will swear no more , for what 
 be word ? yet shalt thou learn that Ayesha hath no false tongue . 

 " so I have swear , and thou , my Holly , art witness to my oath . here , too , 
 be we we d , my husband , with the gloom for bridal canopy - we d till the 
 end of all thing ; here do we write our marriage vow upon the rushing 
 wind which shall bear they up to heaven , and round and continually 
 round this rolling world . 

 " and for a bridal gift I crown thee with my beauty 's starry crown , and 
 endure life , and wisdom without measure , and wealth that none can 
 count . Behold ! the great one of the earth shall creep about thy foot , 
 and its fair woman shall cover up their eye because of the shin 
 glory of thy countenance , and its wise one shall be abase before thee . 
 thou shalt read the heart of man as an open writing , and hither and 
 thither shalt thou lead they as thy pleasure listeth . like that old 
 Sphinx of Egypt shalt thou sit aloft from age to age , and ever shall 
 they cry to thee to solve the riddle of thy greatness that doth not pass 
 away , and ever shalt thou mock they with thy silence ! 

 " Behold ! once more I kiss thee , and by that kiss I give to thee dominion 
 over sea and earth , over the peasant in his hovel , over the monarch in 
 his palace hall , and city crown with tower , and those who breathe 
 therein . Where'er the sun shake out his spear , and the lonesome water 
 mirror up the moon , where'er storm roll , and Heaven 's paint bow arch 
 in the sky - from the pure North clothe in snow , across the middle space 
 of the world , to where the amorous South , lie like a bride upon her 
 blue couch of sea , breathe in sigh make sweet with the odour of 
 myrtle - there shall thy power pass and thy dominion find a home . nor 
 sickness , nor icy - finger fear , nor sorrow , and pale waste of form and 
 mind hover ever o'er humanity , shall so much as shadow thee with the 
 shadow of their wing . as a God shalt thou be , hold good and evil in 
 the hollow of thy hand , and I , even I , I humble myself before thee . 
 such be the power of love , and such be the bridal gift I give unto thee , 
 Kallikrates , my Lord and Lord of All . 

 " and now it be do ; now for thee I loose my virgin zone ; and come 
 storm , come shine , come good , come evil , come life , come death , it 
 never , never can be undo . for , of a truth , that which be , be , and , 
 be do , be do for aye , and can not be alter . I have say - let we 
 hence , that all thing may be accomplish in their order ; " and , take 
 one of the lamp , she advance towards the end of the chamber that be 
 roof in by the sway stone , where she halt . 

 we follow she , and perceive that in the wall of the cone there be a 
 stair , or , to be more accurate , that some project knob of rock have 
 be so shaped as to form a good imitation of a stair . down this Ayesha 
 begin to climb , spring from step to step , like a chamois , and after 
 she we follow with less grace . when we have descend some fifteen 
 or sixteen step we find that they end in a tremendous rocky slope , 
 run first outward and then inwards - like the slope of an invert 
 cone , or tunnel . the slope be very steep , and often precipitous , but 
 it be nowhere impassable , and by the light of the lamp we go down it 
 with no great difficulty , though it be gloomy work enough travel on 
 thus , no one of we know whither , into the dead heart of a volcano . as 
 we go , however , I take the precaution of note our route as well as 
 I could ; and this be not so very difficult , owe to the extraordinary 
 and most fantastic shape of the rock that be strew about , many of 
 which in that dim light look more like the grim face carven upon 
 mediæval gargoyle than ordinary boulder . 

 for a long time we travel on thus , half an hour I should say , till , 
 after we have descend for many hundred of foot , I perceive that we 
 be reach the point of the invert cone . in another minute we be 
 there , and find that at the very apex of the funnel be a passage , so 
 low and narrow that we have to stoop as we creep along it in indian file . 
 after some fifty yard of this creeping , the passage suddenly widen 
 into a cave , so huge that we could see neither the roof nor the side . 
 we only know that it be a cave by the echo of our tread and the perfect 
 quiet of the heavy air . on we go for many minute in absolute awed 
 silence , like lose soul in the depth of Hades , Ayesha 's white and 
 ghost - like form flit in front of we , till once more the place end 
 in a passage which open into a second cavern much small than the 
 first . indeed , we could clearly make out the arch and stony bank of 
 this second cave , and , from their rent and jagged appearance , discover 
 that , like the first long passage down which we have pass through the 
 cliff before we reach the quivering spur , it have , to all appearance , 
 be tear in the bowel of the rock by the terrific force of some 
 explosive gas . at length this cave end in a third passage , through 
 which gleam a faint glow of light . 

 I hear Ayesha give a sigh of relief as this light dawn upon we . 

 " it be well , " she say ; " prepare to enter the very womb of the Earth , 
 wherein she doth conceive the life that ye see bring forth in man and 
 beast - ay , and in every tree and flower . " 

 swiftly she speed along , and after she we stumble as well we might , our 
 heart fill like a cup with mingled dread and curiosity . what be we 
 about to see ? we pass down the tunnel ; strong and strong the light 
 beam , reach we in great flash like the ray from a lighthouse , as 
 one by one they be throw wide upon the darkness of the water . nor be 
 this all , for with the flash come a soul - shake sound like that of 
 thunder and of crash tree . now we be through it , and - oh heaven ! 

 we stand in a third cavern , some fifty foot in length by perhaps as 
 great a height , and thirty wide . it be carpet with fine white sand , 
 and its wall have be wear smooth by the action of I know not what . the 
 cavern be not dark like the other , it be fill with a soft glow of 
 rise - colour light , more beautiful to look on than anything that can 
 be conceive . but at first we see no flash , and hear no more of the 
 thunderous sound . presently , however , as we stand in amaze , gaze at 
 the marvellous sight , and wonder whence the rosy radiance flow , a 
 dread and beautiful thing happen . across the far end of the 
 cavern , with a grind and crash noise - a noise so dreadful and 
 awe - inspiring that we all tremble , and Job actually sink to his 
 knee - there flame out an awful cloud or pillar of fire , like a rainbow 
 many - colour , and like the lightning bright . for a space , perhaps forty 
 second , it flame and roar thus , turn slowly round and round , and 
 then by degree the terrible noise cease , and with the fire it pass 
 away - I know not where - leave behind it the same rosy glow that we have 
 first see . 

 " draw near , draw near ! " cry Ayesha , with a voice of thrilling 
 exultation . " behold the very Fountain and Heart of Life as it beat in 
 the bosom of the great world . behold the substance from which all thing 
 draw their energy , the bright Spirit of the Globe , without which it 
 can not live , but must grow cold and dead as the dead moon . draw near , 
 and wash you in the living flame , and take their virtue into your poor 
 frame in all its virgin strength - not as it now feebly glow within 
 your bosom , filter thereto through all the fine strainer of a 
 thousand intermediate life , but as it be here in the very fount and 
 seat of earthly being . " 

 we follow she through the rosy glow up to the head of the cave , till 
 at last we stand before the spot where the great pulse beat and the 
 great flame pass . and as we go we become sensible of a wild and 
 splendid exhilaration , of a glorious sense of such a fierce intensity of 
 Life that the most buoyant moment of our strength seem flat and tame 
 and feeble beside it . it be the mere effluvium of the flame , the subtle 
 ether that it cast off as it pass , work on we , and make we feel 
 strong as giant and swift as eagle . 

 we reach the head of the cave , and gaze at each other in the glorious 
 glow , and laugh aloud - even Job laugh , and he have not laugh for a 
 week - in the lightness of our heart and the divine intoxication of our 
 brain . I know that I feel as though all the varied genius of which the 
 human intellect be capable have descend upon I . I could have speak 
 in blank verse of shakesperian beauty , all sort of great idea flash 
 through my mind ; it be as though the bond of my flesh have be 
 loosen and leave the spirit free to soar to the empyrean of its native 
 power . the sensation that pour in upon I be indescribable . I seem 
 to live more keenly , to reach to a high joy , and sip the goblet of a 
 subtler think than ever it have be my lot to do before . I be another 
 and most glorify self , and all the avenue of the possible be for a 
 space lay open to the footstep of the Real . 

 then , suddenly , whilst I rejoice in this splendid vigour of a new - find 
 self , from far , far away there come a dreadful muttering noise , that 
 grow and grow to a crash and a roar , which combine in itself all that 
 be terrible and yet splendid in the possibility of sound . Nearer it 
 come , and nearer yet , till it be close upon we , roll down like all 
 the thunder - wheel of heaven behind the horse of the lightning . on 
 it come , and with it come the glorious blinding cloud of many - colour 
 light , and stand before we for a space , turn , as it seem to we , 
 slowly round and round , and then , accompany by its attendant pomp of 
 sound , pass away I know not whither . 

 so astonishing be the wondrous sight that one and all of we , save 
  she , who stand up and stretch her hand towards the fire , sink down 
 before it , and hide our face in the sand . 

 when it be go , Ayesha speak . 

 " now , Kallikrates , " she say , " the mighty moment be at hand . when the 
 great flame come again thou must stand in it . first throw aside thy 
 garment , for it will burn they , though thee it will not hurt . Thou must 
 stand in the flame while thy sens will endure , and when it embrace 
 thee suck the fire down into thy very heart , and let it leap and play 
 around thy every part , so that thou lose no moiety of its virtue . 
 hear thou I , Kallikrates ? " 

 " I hear thee , Ayesha , " answer Leo , " but , of a truth - I be no 
 coward - but I doubt I of that rag flame . how know I that it will 
 not utterly destroy I , so that I lose myself and lose thee also ? 
 nevertheless will I do it , " he add . 

 Ayesha think for a minute , and then say - 

 " it be not wonderful that thou shouldst doubt . tell I , Kallikrates : 
 if thou se I stand in the flame and come forth unharmed , wilt thou 
 enter also ? " 

 " yes , " he answer , " I will enter even if it slay I . I have say that I 
 will enter now . " 

 " and that will I also , " I cry . 

 " what , my Holly ! " she laugh aloud ; " methought that thou wouldst naught 
 of length of day . why , how be this ? " 

 " Nay , I know not , " I answer , " but there be that in my heart that 
 calleth I to taste of the flame and live . " 

 " it be well , " she say . " thou art not altogether lose in folly . see now , 
 I will for the second time bathe I in this living bath . fain would I 
 add to my beauty and my length of day if that be possible . if it be not 
 possible , at the least it can not harm I . 

 " also , " she continue , after a momentary pause , " be there another and 
 a deep cause why I would once again dip I in the flame . when first I 
 taste of its virtue full be my heart of passion and of hatred of 
 that Egyptian Amenartas , and therefore , despite my striving to be rid 
 thereof , have passion and hatred be stamp upon my soul from that sad 
 hour to this . but now it be otherwise . now be my mood a happy mood , and 
 fill be I with the pure part of thought , and so would I ever be . 
 therefore , Kallikrates , will I once more wash and make I pure and 
 clean , and yet more fit for thee . therefore also , when thou dost in turn 
 stand in the fire , empty all thy heart of evil , and let soft contentment 
 hold the balance of thy mind . shake loose thy spirit 's wing , and take 
 thy stand upon the utter verge of holy contemplation ; ay , dream upon thy 
 mother 's kiss , and turn thee towards the vision of the high good that 
 hath ever sweep on silver wing across the silence of thy dream . for 
 from the germ of what thou art in that dread moment shall grow the fruit 
 of what thou shalt be for all unreckoned time . 

 " now prepare thee , prepare ! even as though thy last hour be at hand , 
 and thou wast to cross to the Land of Shadows , and not through the Gates 
 of glory into the realm of Life make beautiful . Prepare , I say ! "

 then come a few moment ' pause , during which Ayesha seem to be 
 gather up her strength for the fiery trial , while we cling to each 
 other , and wait in utter silence . 

 at last , from far far away , come the first murmur of sound , that grow 
 and grow till it begin to crash and bellow in the distance . as she hear 
 it , Ayesha swiftly throw off her gauzy wrap , loosen the golden 
 snake from her kirtle , and then , shake her lovely hair about she like 
 a garment , beneath its cover slip the kirtle off and replace the 
 snaky belt around she and outside the mass of her fall hair . there 
 she stand before we as Eve might have stand before Adam , clothe in nothing 
 but her abundant lock , hold round she by the golden band ; and no word 
 of mine can tell how sweet she look - and yet how divine . Nearer and 
 nearer come the thunder - wheel of fire , and as they come she push one 
 ivory arm through the dark mass of her hair and fling it round Leo 's 
 neck . 

 " oh , my love , my love ! " she murmur , " wilt thou ever know how I have 
 love thee ? " and she kiss he on the forehead , and then go and stand 
 in the pathway of the flame of Life . 

 there be , I remember , to my mind something very touch about her 
 word and that embrace upon the forehead . it be like a mother 's kiss , 
 and seem to convey a benediction with it . 

 on come the crash , rolling noise , and the sound of it be as the 
 sound of a forest be sweep flat by a mighty wind , and then toss 
 up like so much grass , and thunder down a mountain - side . Nearer and 
 near it come ; now flash of light , forerunner of the revolving 
 pillar of flame , be pass like arrow through the rosy air ; and now 
 the edge of the pillar itself appear . Ayesha turn towards it , and 
 stretch out her arm to greet it . on it come very slowly , and lap 
 her round with flame . I see the fire run up her form . I see she lift it 
 with both hand as though it be water , and pour it over her head . I 
 even see she open her mouth and draw it down into her lung , and a dread 
 and wonderful sight it be . 

 then she pause , and stretch out her arm , and stand there quite 
 still , with a heavenly smile upon her face , as though she be the very 
 Spirit of the Flame . 

 the mysterious fire play up and down her dark and rolling lock , 
 twining and twist itself through and around they like thread of 
 golden lace ; it gleam upon her ivory breast and shoulder , from which 
 the hair have slip aside ; it slide along her pillare throat and 
 delicate feature , and seem to find a home in the glorious eye that 
 shine and shine , more brightly even than the spiritual essence . 

 oh , how beautiful she look there in the flame ! no angel out of heaven 
 could have wear a great loveliness . even now my heart faint before 
 the recollection of it , as she stand and smile at our awed face , and 
 I would give half my remain time upon this earth to see she once like 
 that again . 

 but suddenly - more suddenly than I can describe - a kind of change come 
 over her face , a change which I could not define or explain , but none 
 the less a change . the smile vanish , and in its place there come a 
 dry , hard look ; the rounded face seem to grow pinch , as though some 
 great anxiety be leave its impress upon it . the glorious eye , too , 
 lose their light , and , as I think , the form its perfect shape and 
 erectness . 

 I rub my eye , think that I be the victim of some hallucination , 
 or that the refraction from the intense light produce an optical 
 delusion ; and , as I do so , the flame pillar slowly twist and 
 thunder off whithersoever it pass to in the bowel of the great 
 earth , leave Ayesha stand where it have be . 

 as soon as it be go , she step forward to Leo 's side - it seem to 
 I that there be no spring in her step - and stretch out her hand 
 to lay it on his shoulder . I gaze at her arm . where be its wonderful 
 roundness and beauty ? it be get thin and angular . and her face - by 
 Heaven ! - her face be grow old before my eye ! I suppose that Leo 
 see it also ; certainly he recoil a step or two . 

 " what be it , my Kallikrates ? " she say , and her voice - what be the 
 matter with those deep and thrilling note ? they be quite high and 
 crack . 

 " why , what be it - what be it ? " she say confusedly . " I feel daze . 
 surely the quality of the fire hath not alter . can the principle of 
 Life alter ? tell I , Kallikrates , be there aught wrong with my eye ? 
 I see not clear , " and she put her hand to her head and touch she 
 hair - and oh , horror of horror ! - it all fall upon the floor . 

 " oh , look ! - look ! - look ! " shriek Job , in a shrill falsetto of 
 terror , his eye nearly drop out of his head , and foam upon his 
 lip . " look ! - look ! - look ! she be shrivel up ! she be turn into 
 a monkey ! " and down he fall upon the ground , foaming and gnashing in a 
 fit . 

 true enough - I faint even as I write it in the live presence of that

 I know not how long we remain thus . many hour , I suppose . when at

 what have happen to bring this shocking change about ? have the nature

 Well , and then we go . we go , and leave those two in the presence of 
 the very well and spring of life , but gather to the cold company of 
 Death . how lonely they look as they lie there , and how ill assort ! 
 that little heap have be for two thousand year the wise , lovely , 
 proud creature - I can hardly call her woman - in the whole universe . 
 she have be wicked , too , in her way ; but , alas ! such be the frailty

 XXVII 

 we LEAP 

 we pass through the cave without trouble , but when we come to the

 but now a fresh terror star we in the face . it will be remember that

 how be we to cross without the plank ? 

 there be only one answer - we must try and jump it , or else stop there

 eleven and twelve foot I should think , and I have see Leo jump over 
 twenty when he be a young fellow at collage ; but then , think of the

 as we do so the light go out . 

 the difference in our position be a sufficiently remarkable one . 
 below , in the little chamber , we have only hear the roaring of the

 the fact be I do not expect to live another two minute .

 it be early morning - that we could tell by the feel of the sweet air

 " one more effort , Leo , " I gasp , " and we shall reach the slope where

 presently , to my intense relief , I see old billali hurrying towards

 " oh , my Baboon ! my Baboon ! " he cry , " my dear son , be it indeed thee

  She - who - must - be - obey ? " 

 " dead , both dead , " I answer ; " but ask no question ; help we , and give

 over the MOUNTAIN 

 the next thing I recollect be a feeling of the most dreadful stiffness ,

 Billali , who be seat by the side of the improvise bed upon which I 
 be sleep , and thoughtfully stroke his long beard . the sight of 
 he at once bring back to my mind a recollection of all that we have 
 recently pass through , which be accentuate by the vision of poor 
 Leo lie opposite to I , his face knock almost to a jelly , and his 
 beautiful crowd of curl turn from yellow to white ,     and I shut my 
 eye again and groan . 

      curiously enough , Leo 's hair have lately be to some 
  extent regain its colour - that be to say , it be now a 
  yellowish grey , and I be not without hope that it will in 
  time come quite right . - L. H. H. 

 " Thou hast sleep long , my Baboon , " say old Billali . 

 " how long , my father ? " I ask . 

 " a round of the sun and a round of the moon , a day and a night hast thou 
 sleep , and the Lion also . see , he sleepeth yet . " 

 " blessed be sleep , " I answer , " for it swallow up recollection . " 

 " tell I , " he say , " what hath befall you , and what be this strange 
 story of the death of she who dieth not . bethink thee , my son : if this 
 be true , then be thy danger and the danger of the Lion very great - nay , 
 almost be the pot red wherewith ye shall be pot , and the stomach of 
 those who shall eat ye be already hungry for the feast . know thou 
 not that these Amahagger , my child , these dweller in the cave , 
 hate ye ? they hate ye as stranger , they hate ye more because of their 
 brother whom she put to the torment for your sake . assuredly , if once 
 they learn that there be naught to fear from Hiya , from the terrible 
 one - who - must - be - obey , they will slay ye by the pot . but let I hear 
 thy tale , my poor Baboon . " 

 this adjure , I set to work and tell he - not everything , indeed , for 
 I do not think it desirable to do so , but sufficient for my purpose , 
 which be to make he understand that she be really no more , have 
 fall into some fire , and , as I put it - for the real thing would have 
 be incomprehensible to he - be burn up . I also tell he some of the 
 horror we have undergo in effect our escape , and these produce a 
 great impression on he . but I clearly see that he do not believe in 
 the report of Ayesha 's death . he believe indeed that we think 
 that she be dead , but his explanation be that it have suit she to 
 disappear for a while . once , he say , in his father 's time , she have do 
 so for twelve year , and there be a tradition in the country that many 
 century back no one have see she for a whole generation , when she 
 suddenly reappear , and destroy a woman who have assume the position 
 of Queen . I say nothing to this , but only shake my head sadly . alas ! 
 I know too well that Ayesha would appear no more , or at any rate that 
 Billali would never see she again . 

 " and now , " conclude Billali , " what wouldst thou do , my Baboon ? " 

 " Nay , " I say , " I know not , my father . can we not escape from this 
 country ? " 

 he shake his head . 

 " it be very difficult . by K"r ye can not pass , for ye would be see , 
 and as soon as those fierce one find that ye be alone , well , " and 
 he smile significantly , and make a movement as though he be place a 
 hat on his head . " but there be a way over the cliff whereof I once spake 
 to thee , where they drive the cattle out to pasture . then beyond the 
 pasture be three day ' journey through the marsh , and after that 
 I know not , but I have hear that seven day ' journey from thence be 
 a mighty river , which floweth to the black water . if ye could come 
 thither , perchance ye might escape , but how can ye come thither ? " 

 " Billali , " I say , " once , thou know , I do save thy life . now pay 
 back the debt , my father , and save I mine and my friend 's , the Lion 's . 
 it shall be a pleasant thing for thee to think of when thine hour come , 
 and something to set in the scale against the evil doing of thy day , if 
 perchance thou hast do any evil . also , if thou be right , and if she 
 doth but hide herself , surely when she come again she shall reward 
 thee . " 

 " my son the Baboon , " answer the old man , " think not that I have an 
 ungrateful heart . well do I remember how thou didst rescue I when those 
 dog stand by to see I drown . measure for measure will I give thee , 
 and if thou canst be save , surely I will save thee . listen : by dawn 
 to - morrow be prepare , for litter shall be here to bear ye away across 
 the mountain , and through the marsh beyond . this will I do , say 
 that it be the word of she that it be do , and he who obeyeth not the 
 word of she food be he for the hyæna . then when ye have cross the 
 marsh , ye must strike with your own hand , so that perchance , if good 
 fortune go with you , ye may live to come to that black water whereof ye 
 tell I . and now , see , the Lion wake , and ye must eat the food I have 
 make ready for you . " 

 Leo 's condition when once he be fairly arouse prove not to be so 
 bad as might have be expect from his appearance , and we both of we 
 manage to eat a hearty meal , which indeed we need sadly enough . after 
 this we limp down to the spring and bath , and then come back and 
 sleep again till evening , when we once more eat enough for five . Billali 
 be away all that day , no doubt make arrangement about litter and 
 bearer , for we be awaken in the middle of the night by the arrival 
 of a considerable number of man in the little camp . 

 at dawn the old man himself appear , and tell we that he have by use 
  she be dreadful name , though with some difficulty , succeed in get 
 the necessary man and two guide to conduct we across the swamp , and 
 that he urge we to start at once , at the same time announce his 
 intention of accompany we so as to protect we against treachery . I 
 be much touch by this act of kindness on the part of that wily old 
 barbarian towards two utterly defenceless stranger . a three - or in 
 his case , for he would have to return , six - day ' journey through those 
 deadly swamp be no light undertaking for a man of his age , but he 
 consent to do it cheerfully in order to promote our safety . it show 
 that even among those dreadful Amahagger - who be certainly with their 
 gloom and their devilish and ferocious rite by far the most terrible 
 savage that I ever hear of - there be people with kindly heart . of 
 course , self - interest may have have something to do with it . he may have 
 think that she would suddenly reappear and demand an account of we 
 at his hand , but still , allow for all deduction , it be a great 
 deal more than we could expect under the circumstance , and I can only 
 say that I shall for as long as I live cherish a most affectionate 
 remembrance of my nominal parent , old Billali . 

 accordingly , after swallow some food , we start in the litter , 
 feeling , so far as our body go , wonderfully like our old self 
 after our long rest and sleep . I must leave the condition of our mind 
 to the imagination . 

 then come a terrible pull up the cliff . sometimes the ascent be more 
 natural , more often it be a zig - zag roadway cut , no doubt , in the first 
 instance by the old inhabitant of K"r . the Amahagger say they drive 
 their spare cattle over it once a year to pasture outside ; all I know be 
 that those cattle must be uncommonly active on their foot . of course the 
 litter be useless here , so we have to walk . 

 by midday , however , we reach the great flat top of that mighty wall of 
 rock , and grand enough the view be from it , with the plain of K"r , in 
 the centre of which we could clearly make out the pillare ruin of the 
 Temple of Truth to the one side , and the boundless and melancholy marsh 
 on the other . this wall of rock , which have no doubt once form the lip 
 of the crater , be about a mile and a half thick , and still cover with 
 clinker . nothing grow there , and the only thing to relieve our eye be 
 occasional pool of rain - water   for rain have lately fall   wherever 
 there be a little hollow . over the flat crest of this mighty rampart we 
 go , and then come the descent , which , if not so difficult a matter 
 as the getting up , be still sufficiently break - neck , and take we till 
 sunset . that night , however , we camp in safety upon the mighty slope 
 that roll away to the marsh beneath . 

 on the following morning , about eleven o'clock , begin our dreary journey 
 across those awful sea of swamp which I have already describe . 

 for three whole day , through stench and mire , and the all - prevail 
 flavour of fear , do our bearer struggle along , till at length we come 
 to open roll ground quite uncultivated , and mostly treeless , but 
 cover with game of all sort , which lie beyond that most desolate , 
 and without guide utterly impracticable , district . and here on the 
 follow morning we bade farewell , not without some regret , to old 
 Billali , who stroke his white beard and solemnly bless we . 

 " farewell , my son the Baboon , " he say , " and farewell to thee too , oh 
 Lion . I can do no more to help you . but if ever ye come to your country , 
 be advise , and venture no more into land that ye know not , lest ye 
 come back no more , but leave your white bone to mark the limit of your 
 journeying . farewell once more ; often shall I think of you , nor wilt 
 thou forget I , my Baboon , for though thy face be ugly thy heart be 
 true . " and then he turn and go , and with he go the tall and 
 sullen - look bearer , and that be the last that we see of the 
 Amahagger . we watch they wind away with the empty litter like a 
 procession bear dead man from a battle , till the mist from the marsh 
 gather round they and hide they , and then , leave utterly desolate in the 
 vast wilderness , we turn and gaze round we and at each other . 

 three week or so before four man have enter the marsh of K"r , and 
 now two of we be dead , and the other two have go through adventure 
 and experience so strange and terrible that death himself hath not a 
 more fearful countenance . three week - and only three week ! truly time 
 should be measure by event , and not by the lapse of hour . it seem 
 like thirty year since we see the last of our whale - boat . 

 " we must strike out for the Zambesi , Leo , " I say , " but God know if we 
 shall ever get there . " 

 Leo nod . he have become very silent of late , and we start with 
 nothing but the clothe we stand in , a compass , our revolver and 
 express rifle , and about two hundred round of ammunition , and so end 
 the history of our visit to the ancient ruin of mighty and imperial 
 K"r . 

 as for the adventure that subsequently befell we , strange and varied 
 as they be , I have , after deliberation , determine not to record they 
 here . in these page I have only try to give a short and clear account 
 of an occurrence which I believe to be unprecedented , and this I have 
 do , not with a view to immediate publication , but merely to put 
 on paper while they be yet fresh in our memory the detail of our 
 journey and its result , which will , I believe , prove interesting to 
 the world if ever we determine to make they public . this , as at present 
 advise , we do not intend should be do during our joint life . 

 for the rest , it be of no public interest , resemble as it do the 
 experience of more than one central african traveller . suffice it to 
 say , that we do , after incredible hardship and privation , reach the 
 Zambesi , which prove to be about a hundred and seventy mile south 
 of where Billali leave we . there we be for six month imprison by 
 a savage tribe , who believe we to be supernatural being , chiefly on 
 account of Leo 's youthful face and snow - white hair . from these people we 
 ultimately escape , and , cross the Zambesi , wander off southward , 
 where , when on the point of starvation , we be sufficiently fortunate 
 to fall in with a half - cast portuguese elephant - hunter who have follow 
 a troop of elephant far inland than he have ever be before . this 
 man treat we most hospitably , and ultimately through his assistance 
 we , after innumerable suffering and adventure , reach Delagoa Bay , 
 more than eighteen month from the time when we emerge from the marsh 
 of K"r , and the very next day manage to catch one of the steamboat 
 that run round the Cape to England . our journey home be a prosperous 
 one , and we set our foot on the quay at Southampton exactly two year 
 from the date of our departure upon our wild and seemingly ridiculous 
 quest , and I now write these last word with Leo lean over my 
 shoulder in my old room in my college , the very same into which some 
 two - and - twenty year ago my poor friend Vincey come stumble on the 
 memorable night of his death , bear the iron chest with he . 



 and that be the end of this history so far as it concern science and 
 the outside world . what its end will be as regard Leo and myself be 
 more than I can guess at . but we feel that be not reach yet . a story 
 that begin more than two thousand year ago may stretch a long way into 
 the dim and distant future . 

 be Leo really a reincarnation of the ancient Kallikrates of whom the 
 inscription tell ? or be Ayesha deceive by some strange hereditary 
 resemblance ? the reader must form his own opinion on this as on many 
 other matter . I have mine , which be that she make no such mistake . 

 often I sit alone at night , star with the eye of the mind into the 
 blackness of unborn time , and wonder in what shape and form the great 
 drama will be finally develop , and where the scene of its next act 
 will be lay . and when that final development ultimately occur , as I 
 have no doubt it must and will occur , in obedience to a fate that never 
 swerve and a purpose that can not be alter , what will be the part 
 play therein by that beautiful Egyptian Amenartas , the Princess of the 
 royal race of the Pharaohs , for the love of whom the Priest Kallikrates 
 break his vow to isis , and , pursue by the inexorable vengeance of the 
 outraged Goddess , flee down the coast of Libya to meet his doom at K"r ?
